She groaned at the sound of a familiar voice. Of course, of all the people to still be here…

Tori forced a smile onto her face before turning to see Nicky walking toward her, but her expression immediately shifted to a confused frown when she saw the little boy walking beside her. His eyes were red and his face was splotchy, like he had been crying.

“Hey,” she greeted, looking from the boy to Nicky in confusion.

“This is my brother, Ollie,” Nicky told her. “Ollie, this is Tori.”

The boy didn’t speak to her. Instead he started rocking in place, his arms wrapped tightly around his middle.

“Is he… okay?” Tori asked.

“He’s autistic,” Nicky explained. “He got startled by another kid at dismissal today and is having a hard time right now. Isn’t that right, Ollie?”

The boy managed a small nod, but he kept rocking and didn’t meet Tori’s eyes.

“What are you still doing here?” Nicky asked. “Is everything okay?”

“Yeah, I’m just waiting for my mom,” Tori explained. “There was an emergency at the clinic and she’s running late.”

“Oh, shit, I hope everything’s okay,” Nicky said with a frown.

“I’m sure it—” Tori was cut off by her phone ringing. Instead of her mother’s number, the contact for the veterinary office flashed on the screen. “I bet this is her, could you give me a minute?” Nicky nodded and Tori answered the call. “Mami?”

“Tori?” said an unfamiliar voice. “This is Rahne, I work with your mom.”

“Hi,” Tori greeted. “Is everything okay?”

“She’s with a patient right now,” Rahne explained. “It’s going to be a few hours before she can leave and go home. She wanted me to tell you to go ask Mrs. Maximoff for a ride, or Deputy Wu-Gulliver.”

“Oh, yeah, I guess I can find a ride,” Tori replied.

“I can give you a ride,” Nicky interrupted.

Tori looked from Nicky to her brother. “You sure?”

“Yeah, he’s okay now,” Nicky assured her. “I mean, he’s still self-soothing, but this is good. I can give you a ride home, no problem.”

Tori bit her lip, considering.

“Tori? You still there?” Rahne called on the phone.

“Can you tell mom that I’m getting a ride with Nicky?” Tori asked. “She knows her, I think, she’s—”

“Oh, the intern!” Rahne said, her tone delighted. “Yes, I’ll let her know.”

“Thanks,” Tori said, then hung up the phone. “Um… Thank you.”

“No problem,” Nicky said with a smile. “My truck’s right over here.”

Ollie climbed into the backseat of the truck and strapped himself into a booster seat. Tori got in the front passenger’s seat and looked around as Nicky started the ignition. The floorboard was filled with coffee cups, energy drink cans, and snack wrappers. Several pairs of sunglasses were hung on the front visors, as well as ticket stubs from rodeos and concerts.

“Sorry for the mess,” Nicky said nervously.

“It’s fine,” Tori assured her. “Turn left, by the way.”

“Got it,” Nicky replied with a nod.

They drove in silence for a few minutes. Nicky didn’t turn on any music, probably because of Ollie. Tori stared out the window as they drove through the small town.

“Nicky?” Ollie called from the backseat.

“Yeah, bud?”

“Can we get milkshakes?”

Nicky’s expression softened and she looked at Tori. “Would you mind? It won’t take long, and it always cheers him up after a meltdown.”

“No, that’s fine,” Tori agreed.

Nicky turned onto one of the side streets and parked in front of a small restaurant. Tori followed the two of them inside and to the back counter where a large ice cream freezer was sitting.

“This place has the best ice cream flavors,” Nicky whispered conspiratorially. “Hey, Monica.”

The girl behind the counter turned to them with a smile. “Hey, Nicky. Who’s your friend?”

Tori opened her mouth to introduce herself, but no sound came out. The girl behind the counter was beautiful. She had big brown eyes, curly black hair that was pulled into a ponytail, and when she smiled Tori felt like her stomach was full of butterflies.

“Uh— Hi,” she managed, finally.

Nicky looked between Tori and the other girl knowingly. “This is Tori. She just moved here from California.”

“Cool,” Monica said, smiling at her.

“Y— Yeah. Cool,” Tori stuttered.

Monica looked at her expectantly for a minute, but Tori couldn’t make herself speak. Finally the other girl looked back at Nicky.

“You guys want the usual?” she asked.

“Yeah, a chocolate peanut butter swirl milkshake for Ollie and mocha swirl for me,” Nicky replied. “What do you want, Tori? My treat.”

Tori finally found her voice. “Oh, you don’t have to do that, I can buy my own.”

“No, let me,” Nicky insisted. “Just don’t get anything with tree nuts— Ollie’s allergic.”

“Okay, um…” Tori looked at the flavors in the freezer. “I don’t know… Any suggestions?”

“Depends on what you like,” Monica said, already scooping ice cream into a metal cup to make one of the milkshakes. “My favorite is the lemon meringue ice cream with blueberry swirl.”

“Oh, that sounds really good, actually,” Tori said. “I’ll try that.”

“Alright, I’ll get those ready for you,” Monica said, her smile sending the butterflies buzzing in Tori’s stomach again.

“Wow.”

Tori jumped at the sound of Nicky’s voice right beside her. She had almost forgotten the other girl was there. Ollie had wandered to the other side of the restaurant and was playing with some kind of pinball machine. Nicky just looked at Tori knowingly, a slight grin on her face.

“What?”

“Nothing,” Nicky said. “You’re just so flustered.”

“I am not,” Tori grumbled, dragging her toe across the tile floor.

“You like her,” Nicky whispered, conspiratorially, nudging her elbow.

“That’s none of your business,” Tori told her.

“I’m just saying, you should go for it,” Nicky said. “Monica’s really nice.”

“I don’t even know if she’s into girls,” Tori whispered.

“Well, there’s only one way to know,” Nicky said with a wink. She went to pay for their shakes, constantly looking back at Tori with a knowing look. Once she had finished paying, she gave Tori one more look, but Tori just shook her head slightly. Nicky rolled her eyes and handed her one of the milkshakes. “It was good to see you, Monica.”

“Good to see you guys,” Monica replied. She turned toward Tori. “It was nice to meet you, Tori. Maybe I’ll see you around?”

“Yeah, uh, sure,” Tori stuttered.

“C’mon, Ollie,” Nicky called, and she passed the boy his milkshake as they left.

“This is really good,” Tori said, sipping on her milkshake as they left the restaurant.

“They have the best ice cream in town,” Nicky told her. “Monica’s moms are both military, and her grandparents own the restaurant.”

“I’ll have to pay you back for this,” Tori told her.

“I told you not to worry about it.”

Tori turned to her, stopping her in her tracks on the sidewalk. “Why are you being so nice to me?”

Nicky’s eyes widened. “What do you mean?”

“You’re driving me home, you bought me a milkshake,” Tori explained. “You’re being nice, which makes no sense after you called me a freak last week.”

“That’s not nice,” Ollie remarked, sipping his milkshake a few feet away.

“Ollie, get in the truck,” Nicky instructed. She sighed and looked back at Tori. “I don’t think you’re a freak.”

“Then why say it?” Tori asked.

“I don’t know,” Nicky replied, looking at her own feet and scuffing her boot against the concrete. “Morgan said it and I was just agreeing with her. But I don’t actually think that, I just didn’t want to start something with her.”

“That’s really stupid,” Tori huffed.

“I’m not stupid!” Nicky argued.

“I’m not saying you’re stupid, just that what you did was stupid,” Tori corrected. She studied Nicky for a minute. “Why do you just go along with whatever she says, anyway?”

Nicky sighed and leaned against the hood of her truck. “I don’t know. Morgan’s been my friend since we were in, like, fourth grade. I don’t want to throw away a friendship that’s lasted that long over a stupid disagreement over some new kid I barely even know.”

“But you’re being nice to me now,” Tori said, trying to make sense of Nicky’s actions.

“Well, yeah,” Nicky replied. “You don’t actually seem that bad.”

“Thanks… I think,” Tori replied.

“And… I kind of do have an ulterior motive,” Nicky admitted. “I met your mom at my internship and she’s, like, one of the coolest people ever. I don’t want her to think I’m a terrible person because I was mean to you.”

“So you’re only being nice so that I won’t tattle on you to my mom? Are we five?”

“No— Well, yes, kind of,” Nicky shrugged. “But I was kind of hoping we could, I don’t know, maybe start over?”

Tori eyed her, considering her options. “You know, everyone says you’re kind of a bitch.”

“Oh, I definitely am,” Nicky nodded. “But I try to only be a bitch to people who deserve it.”

“And I don’t deserve it?”

“Not so far. Which means that I really am sorry that I was a bitch and called you a freak on your first day.”

Tori sipped her milkshake. “You know you don’t have to bribe me to be my friend.”

“Well, the bribery wasn’t for that, actually,” Nicky said, standing up straight and heading around to the driver’s side of the truck. “The bribery was for when I ask you for help with pre-calculus.”

Tori climbed into the truck. “I might be able to help you with that.”

“Oh my god, thank you so much,” Nicky squealed as she started the ignition. “I’m like one bad quiz grade away from failing and my mom would literally kill me if I got an F.”

“Nicky,” Ollie called from the backseat.

“Sorry we made you wait, bud. What’s up?” Nicky asked.

“Did you make a new friend?”

“Sort of,” Nicky replied.

Ollie’s face crinkled in confusion. “Sort of? How do you have a sort of friend?”

“Yes, Ollie, we’re friends,” Tori told him.

“Oh, good,” he said, clearly pleased. “Good job, Nicky.”

“Thanks, bud,” Nicky chuckled.

“Do you wanna be my friend, too, Ollie?” Tori asked.

“You’re too old to be my friend,” Ollie replied. “You’re old enough to be my sister.”

“Well… yeah,” Tori replied, confused.

“You can be my sister, like Nicky,” Ollie declared.

“Ollie, that’s not how that works,” Nicky argued.

“Tori, if you’re my sister now, will you come over and see my chickens sometime?” he asked, ignoring Nicky’s correction.

Tori looked at Nicky, who looked just as confused as she did.

“Sure, I’d like that,” Tori replied.

“Yay,” Ollie laughed. “I like having two sisters.”

Tori looked at Nicky again, and Nicky just shrugged. “I’m not arguing with him. Maybe our mom can explain later, but I don’t want him to have another meltdown.”

Tori turned around in her seat and sipped her milkshake. “Guess we’re sisters now.”

“Guess so.”

Tori had just sat down to dinner with her grandfather when Rio finally came through the door, looking absolutely worn out. She wasn’t wearing the clothes she had worn to work that day, but instead had on a pair of gray sweatpants and a blue scrub top. She didn’t speak to them, just gave them a haggard wave before disappearing into the bathroom. A few minutes later, they heard the shower going.

“Looks like she had a rough day,” Mateo noted, spooning a pile of rice onto Tori’s plate.

“Yeah, I’d say,” Tori agreed.

“How about you, nieta? How was your day?”

“It was good,” Tori replied. “I got an A on my pre-calc quiz.”

“Muy bien, nieta, muy bien,” Mateo praised. He shook his head proudly. “You’re a smart girl, Tori. Just like tu madre, si? I’m proud of you.”

“Gracias, Tito,” Tori replied with a grin.

“What about your classmates?” Mateo asked. “Are you getting along with everyone? Have you made any friends?”

“I get along with everyone fine,” Tori said with a shrug. “And I’ve made a few friends.”

“That’s good,” Mateo nodded. “What about boys, hmm?”

Tori’s stomach immediately dropped. “I mean, some of my friends are boys. Billy showed me around school, and his boyfriend Teddy is super nice, too. I have PE and health with him.”

Mateo frowned. “That’s not what I mean, nieta. Aren’t there any nice boys that you might be interested in dating?”

“Tito… I don’t really like boys,” Tori mumbled. “I thought Mami told you that.”

“Oh,” Mateo said, clearing his throat. “She mentioned it, yes.”

Tori frowned. “Then why are you asking about boys?”

“Well, I just thought you might’ve changed your mind, that’s all,” Mateo replied. “The boys here are different from the boys in California.”

“Not really,” Tori said, her tone colored with disgust. She always thought her grandfather was accepting of same-sex couples, and Rio had never mentioned him having a problem with her being a lesbian, so Tori didn’t understand why he was being like this. “But I did meet this girl today that was pretty. Like… really pretty.”

Mateo’s frown deepened. “Is that who drove you home today?”

“No, that was just a friend,” Tori replied. “Speaking of, if it’s okay with Mami, I’m going to her house tomorrow after school to help her with her pre-calc homework.”

“You can ask her when she gets out of the bathroom, I suppose,” Mateo told her. “Just remember, I need you to come home and help exercise and feed Luna.”

“Don’t worry, I’ll be back,” Tori assured him. “Nicky has chores that she has to do, too.”

“Is that your friend’s name, Nicky?” Mateo asked.

“Yeah, Nicky Harkness,” Tori replied, taking a bite of rice and beans.

“What?” Mateo shouted. His fork clattered against his plate as he threw it down.

Tori’s eyes widened at her grandfather’s abrupt loudness. “What?”

“You’re friends with a Harkness?” Mateo asked, still shouting.

“I mean, we’re not besties, but—”

“No,” Mateo said firmly. “No granddaughter of mine is going to be friends with some lying, manipulative, stealing—”

“What are you talking about?” Tori asked.

“Don’t argue with me!” Mateo shouted, rising to his feet.

“I’m not arguing, I just don’t understand,” Tori replied, tears welling up in her eyes. Her heart was pounding in her chest and she felt like she might throw up. Her grandfather had never spoken to her like this before.

“They’re all the same,” Mateo told her. “You will not associate yourself with them, Victoria, I forbid it.”

“Who’s all the same?” Tori asked.

“Harknesses!” Mateo shouted. “A den of vipers. They’re all a bunch of liars and thieves. I thought Jim Harkness was the worst, but after what his granddaughter did to your mother—”

“That’s enough.”

Rio stood on the opposite side of the room, her hair wrapped in a towel, dressed in a t-shirt and pajama pants. She hadn’t raised her voice, but something in her tone made Tori feel as if the temperature of the room had dropped at least ten degrees in an instant. Rio stepped around the foot of the sofa-bed and crossed the room to where they were in the kitchen, stopping just a few steps away from where Mateo stood.

“You are my father, and I love you, but you will never speak to my daughter like that again,” Rio said, her voice still low. “¿Me entiendes papi?”

“Ella es mi nieta,” Mateo argued.

“And she’s my daughter,” Rio replied. “Tori, take your plate and go eat in your room.”

“But—”

“No buts, mija,” Rio said. “And close the door. I need to talk to your abuelo.”

Tori nodded, picked up her plate and her drink, and made her way down the narrow hallway. She closed the door behind her and sat at the desk to eat. Inside his enclosure, Draco stared at her with beady eyes. Even with the door closed, she could still make out the muffled sound of raised voices, mainly her grandfather’s. She knew that they were arguing, but Tori didn’t understand what they were arguing about. She didn’t understand what her grandfather said about Nicky’s family. Tori thought she was a pretty smart kid, and her grades definitely reflected that, but she still couldn’t understand it.

She pushed around the food on her plate, occasionally forcing herself to eat a small bite, for the next ten minutes or so. Finally there was a knock at the door.

“Can I come in?” Rio called, cracking the door just a smidge.

“Yeah— Yes,” Tori replied.

Rio came in and sat on the edge of Tori’s bed. Her hair had come down from the towel, and it hung damp around her shoulders. She looked tired, more tired than Tori could ever remember seeing her.

“I’m sorry your grandfather raised his voice at you,” Rio said. “You did nothing wrong, and even if you had, he shouldn’t have yelled at you.”

Tori’s brow wrinkled in confusion. “Shouldn’t he be the one apologizing for that, not you?”

“It’ll be a cold day in hell before Mateo Vidal apologizes for anything,” Rio muttered. “Your grandfather is the kind of man who believes that because the loudest person in the room usually wins arguments, that must mean that the loudest person is always right.”

“But that’s not—”

“Yes, I know,” Rio sighed. “But I’ve talked to him, and hopefully he understands that he’s not to speak to you that way again. If he has an issue with you, he can talk to me, and I’ll handle any discipline that needs to happen.”

“But I didn’t do anything,” Tori frowned.

“I know, mija, I know,” Rio assured her.

“I don’t understand why he was so upset,” Tori said, her eyes welling up with tears again. She wiped them away angrily. She was an angry crier, and she hated it.

Rio stared at her for a moment, then sighed and laid back on her bed. She patted the mattress beside her, and Tori crawled onto the bed beside her. They both lay on their backs, side by side, looking up at the ceiling.

“Tito said you got a ride home with someone with the last name Harkness?”

“Yeah, and then he freaked out,” Tori said. “What’s his deal?”

“It’s a bit of a long story,” Rio told her. “When Tito was a young man, he worked for this rancher named James Harkness. The Harkness family owns the biggest ranch in the area, always has, for over a hundred years. Anyway, Tito worked as a ranch hand on the Harkness ranch since he was fifteen years old, and he learned how to be a horse trainer. He got to know Mr. Harkness, respected him. But after he got married, Tito didn’t want to just work on the ranch anymore. He wanted to buy his own land and start a horse training business. Nothing big, you know, but he wanted to own something of his own.

“Well, this property came up for sale, and your tito went to the bank to apply for a loan. He was still pretty young, didn’t have much credit. The bank asked for proof of income, and they wanted a character reference. Well, Tito knew that Mr. Harkness was one of the most respected men in Westview, so he went and asked him to be his character reference. Mr. Harkness agreed, but in the end, Tito wasn’t approved for the loan. He was devastated, but life went on. And then a few months later, Tito found out that Mr. Harkness had lied to the bank when he gave the character reference.”

“But why would he lie about Tito?” Tori asked.

“He lied because he wanted to buy the land himself,” Rio replied.

“So that’s why Tito said Harknesses are liars and thieves,” Tori surmised.

“Yes,” Rio nodded. “He’s hated the whole family ever since then.”

“Tito said something else,” Tori said. “He said Mr. Harkness’s granddaughter did something to you. What did she do to you?”

Rio turned her head toward her and reached up to run her fingers through Tori’s hair. “I’ll tell you when you’re older.”

“But Mami,” Tori whined.

“Some things are my business, mija,” Rio said. She sat up with a groan, her bones popping loud enough that Tori could hear them.

“You okay?” Tori asked.

“Yeah, just had a really rough day.” Rio looked down at her. “I trust your judgment of other people, Tori, but maybe stay away from the Harknesses for now. Okay?”

“That’s not fair,” Tori whined.

“You’ll understand when you’re older,” Rio assured her. She stood from the bed and looked around. “Have you finished your homework?”

Tori sighed. “Almost.”

“Alright, well, get to work,” Rio said. “I’m probably going to hit the hay early, so I’ll talk to you in the morning.”

“Okay.”

“Love you, mija.”

Tori looked at her mother, at the dark circles under her eyes and the lines at the corners of her mouth. “Love you, too, Mami.”

Chapter 8: Nicky

Nicky was having a good day.

She had started her morning early, feeding the two calves that she had named Ivy and Betty, before taking Scratchy out to the pasture for turnout. After school she planned on exercising him and practicing on the barrels a few times. She was supposed to run in a local jackpot barrel race event in two weeks, so she had to spend every free minute working with him. There were still plenty of things they could improve on, but they were already starting to fall into a groove, and Nicky could feel it in her bones that he was going to be the perfect horse for her.

Remi had made beignets to go along with their sausage and eggs for breakfast— Nicky’s favorite. Her hair actually cooperated with being straightened. She had time to get a coffee before her internship that morning. She had shadowed Dr. Vidal at the vet clinic, and she had gotten an okay for Tori to come over after school to help her with pre-calc. All in all, a very good morning.

She should’ve known it wouldn’t last.

“And that’s why we’re not talking to Kate anymore.”

Nicky looked up from the Punnett square she was filling in. “Huh?”

Morgan scowled at her. “Seriously? You weren’t even paying attention?”

“I was doing my work,” Nicky groused. As soon as she got to biology class, Morgan had launched into a tirade about her latest argument with Tommy.

“Wally told Barry, who told Iris, and Iris told Felicity, and Felicity told Ava, and Ava told Morgan that Tommy and Kate were sitting together on the bleachers at track practice last week,” Cassie told her, her tone monotonous.

Nicky looked from Cassie’s bored face to Morgan’s furious expression. “Okay. And?”

“She’s clearly trying to get with my boyfriend,” Morgan exclaimed. The students at the next table looked up at that, then immediately went back to their work when Nicky glared at them.

“That doesn’t make any sense,” Nicky said, keeping her voice low. “Kate doesn’t even like Tommy.”

“How do you know?” Morgan demanded.

Because she still likes Yelena, is what Nicky wanted to say, but she knew that wouldn’t go over well either.

“Kate is our friend,” she said instead. “She wouldn’t do that to you. And you know she’s on the archery team, and they practice at the same time as track. They were probably just taking a break together.”

“But why were they sitting together?” Morgan asked.

“They have classes together,” Nicky reminded her, exasperated. “Plus, Tommy hangs out with us at lunch. So it makes sense that they would talk when they see each other at practice.”

“Tommy hangs out with me at lunch,” Morgan said.

“Possessive, much?” Nicky muttered, looking back down at her worksheet. Cassie held back her laughter with a snort, but Morgan hadn’t fully heard her.

“What was that?” Morgan demanded.

“I was just saying that talking to someone doesn’t constitute cheating,” Nicky said. “And it doesn’t seem like a good enough reason to break up a friendship.”

“Well, you don’t get to decide that,” Morgan declared. “I’m not friends with her anymore.”

“Okay, fine, whatever,” Nicky huffed. “But you’re not going to tell me that I can’t be friends with her.”

“You can decide that for yourself,” Morgan said haughtily. “But just know, if you’re friends with her, you’re not friends with me.”

Nicky rolled her eyes. Thankfully the bell rang for lunch before the conversation could continue. Nicky packed up her things and headed toward the cafeteria, not waiting for Morgan or Cassie. She picked up her lunch tray and went to sit at their usual spot, where Kate and Tommy were already sitting waiting for them.

“Just so you know, Morgan’s in a mood,” Nicky warned them.

Tommy groaned. “Again?”

“What happened this time?” Kate asked.

“She thinks that you,” Nicky pointed at Kate, “are trying to get with him,” she pointed at Tommy.

“Ew,” Kate said, sticking her tongue out in disgust. “Why would she think that?”

“I don’t know, but that’s what she thinks,” Nicky shrugged. “So just… brace yourselves.”

Cassie took the seat beside Nicky and a moment later Morgan appeared, standing over the end of the table.

“You need to move,” she said, glaring at Kate.

“Morgan, I don’t know what you think happened, but—” Kate began.

“Baby, this is crazy,” Tommy said.

“Don’t call me crazy!” Morgan exclaimed. She pointed at Kate. “She needs to go.”

“Morgan, you know I’d never try anything with your boyfriend. We’re friends,” Kate tried again.

“Not anymore,” Morgan said, looking down her nose at Kate. “Now move.”

Kate’s mouth opened and closed as she tried to form an argument, but couldn’t. She looked around the table. Cassie looked at her sympathetically while Nicky just kept her head down. Tommy looked furious, but even he didn’t speak up for her.

Kate finally nodded. “Fine. Whatever. Fuck you guys.”

She stood and stormed away from the table, carrying her plate with her.

“Kate!”

Nicky looked up at the familiar voice. On the opposite side of the cafeteria, Tori was waving at Kate, beckoning her toward her table. Kate’s expression turned confused as she made her way over to them. Tori said something that Nicky couldn’t make out, then Kate burst into laughter. Kate sat down next to Yelena, and Nicky could see Yelena’s cheeks flush pink all the way across the lunch room.

“See?” Tommy said to Morgan, his voice pulling Nicky’s attention back to her own table. “There’s no way Kate would’ve been interested in me, because she’s still into Yelena.”

Morgan’s face pinched in irritation. “Whatever. I don’t want to hang out with someone like that anyway.”

Nicky’s irritation flared. “Someone like what, Morgan?”

“Can you guys just drop it?” Cassie exclaimed. “Stop fighting, geez. We’re supposed to be friends.”

Nicky bit her tongue. Cassie was the nicest person in their friend group by far, which meant she was often the peacekeeper. Nicky would hold her tongue for now, for her.

“Sorry,” Nicky muttered, taking a bite of her lunch.

Morgan didn’t apologize, but that wasn’t a surprise, because she never did.

 

Tori was already seated at her desk when Nicky got to pre-calc. Nicky tossed her bag into the floor under her desk and took her seat.

“What happened with Kate and Morgan?” Tori asked as soon as Nicky had sat down.

Nicky sighed and quickly gave her a synopsis. Tori’s nose wrinkled with disgust at the retelling.

“She’s unhinged,” Tori declared.

Nicky snorted. “She’s… possessive."

“Might as well just piss on him to mark her territory if she’s gonna be that big of a bitch,” Tori remarked.

Nicky couldn’t help the smirk that tugged at the corner of her lips. “Anyway, I’m glad you invited Kate to sit with you guys.”

Tori shrugged. “Yelena’s still head over heels for her, so it was a no-brainer.” She bit her lip, then looked at Nicky intently. “You could come sit with us, too, you know.”

Nicky’s pencil froze above her paper. “You think?”

“Yeah, totally,” Tori replied. “As long as you don’t mind hanging out with the freaks.”

Dr. Strange let out a long shhhhhh and glared at them from the front of the room. Nicky went back to writing her notes, though she was just getting more and more confused with each line.

“Hey,” she whispered, “are you still good to come over after school and help me with this stuff?”

Tori bit her lip. “Um… I can’t, actually.”

“What?” Nicky exclaimed, and Dr. Strange shushed her again. “Please, Tori. I’m dying here.”

“My mom doesn’t want me to,” Tori told her. “Something about my grandpa not liking your family or whatever.”

Nicky’s brow furrowed in confusion. “But I just asked her this morning and she said it was okay.”

Tori also looked confused. “What?”

“Yeah, I asked her this morning at my internship,” Nicky replied.

“But last night she said…”

“Maybe text her and ask?” Nicky proposed hopefully.

Tori looked around conspiratorially before pulling her cell phone out of her backpack. She sent a quick text under the desk before putting her phone back into her bag.

“I’ll check for an answer after class,” she assured Nicky.

“Girls, if I have to ask you to be quiet again, I’m moving you to different seats,” Dr. Strange warned.

Tori checked her phone during the class change, but Dr. Vidal hadn’t replied to her message. Once they got to PE, Tori automatically joined Teddy on the basketball court. Before Nicky could decide if she wanted to join them, Morgan appeared beside her.

“I can’t believe Kate chose those weirdos over us,” Morgan said as they stretched.

Nicky looked at her with confusion. “Morgan, you’re the one that told her you didn’t want to be friends anymore, after you accused her of trying to steal your boyfriend.”

“Yeah, but she could’ve fought harder to stay friends with us,” Morgan argued, feigning upset. “Guess she wasn’t that good of a friend to start with.”

Nicky rolled her eyes. Thankfully Coach Danvers chose that moment to blow the whistle to start class. They were running the Pacer test today, and while there were few things Nicky hated more than running, she thought that for once she actually preferred running to listening to her friend complain.

Once they were all sweaty and exhausted, they returned to the locker room to change. Nicky was adjusting her blouse when Tori appeared beside her.

“Mom replied, and she said yes,” she announced. “I don’t know why she changed her mind, and I’m not going to ask.”

“Awesome,” Nicky replied with a grin.

“Ew, freak, why are you talking to us?”

Nicky bit back a groan as Morgan joined her again.

“I wasn’t talking to you, I was talking to Nicky,” Tori replied with a scowl.

“Well, she doesn’t want to talk to you,” Morgan said. “So get lost.”

“Hey,” Nicky spoke up. “You don’t get to speak for me, Morgan.”

“Nicky, why are you even wasting your time—”

“Because she’s helping me with my pre-calc,” Nicky told her. “And because Tori’s actually a pretty cool person.”

“But she hangs out with those—”

“Call me and my friends freaks one more time,” Tori said, her hands clenching into fists at her side.

“Oh, and what are you gonna do about it? Hit me?” Morgan teased.

“Stop being such a bitch, Morgan,” Nicky said.

Morgan crossed her arms over her chest. “If you’re friends with the freaks, you’re not friends with me, Nicky. So pick—”

“I pick them,” Nicky replied simply.

Morgan’s eyes widened in surprise. “But—”

“You’re a bitch and a homophobe and a bully,” Nicky said. “I honestly don’t know why I’ve stayed your friend for this long.”

“But… You can’t do this,” Morgan argued.

“Watch me,” Nicky said, just as the bell rang. “You ready to go, Tori?”

“Yeah, I’m ready,” Tori replied, a wide grin on her face.

 

Chapter 9: Agatha

Chapter Summary

Agatha meets Nicky’s new friend and has a startling realization

Agatha stared at the riverbed in front of her. She had just ridden to this spot days before and hadn’t noticed anything amiss, but now the water level was noticeably lower, and she didn’t know why. They weren’t in a drought, and there hadn’t been any seismic activity or landslides recently.

“What the hell?” she said, leaning against the side-by-side.

“That’s what I said,” Lilia replied. “Then I went upriver. C’mon.”

Agatha sat in the passenger seat of the vehicle and Lilia took off, following the river all the way to the edge of Agatha’s property. Once there they parked the side-by-side and climbed over the fence to continue on foot.

“This is Stark’s property,” Agatha said. It wasn’t a question, but Lilia nodded in confirmation anyway.

They stuck to the high ground and the treeline, finally coming to an overlook. Lilia handed her a pair of binoculars, and Agatha peered down at the plains below them. She could see several trucks and construction equipment parked in the field, just beside the river.

“Are they building a dam?” Agatha asked, squinting into the binoculars.

“Sure looks that way to me,” Lilia nodded. “Whatever they’re doing, it’s obstructing the flow of water.”

“I’ll have Jen look for any permits,” Agatha replied. “He can’t just dam up a whole river. My cattle aren’t the only thing that rely on that water, there’s wildlife, too.”

“What do we do in the meantime?” Lilia asked.

It wasn’t a secret that Tony Stark wanted to buy the Harkness Ranch, he’d offered to buy it multiple times before. Stark wouldn’t stop at her ranch. He wanted to buy every ranch. He wanted to own the world. Not because he had any use for the land or the cattle, no. Stark wanted to build strip malls and housing developments and tech warehouses, all with his name stamped on the side. Agatha would be damned before she let that happen.

“I’ll reach out to Fish and Game, and the wildlife conservationists,” Agatha said finally. “Even if he has his permits in order, which I doubt he does, I bet they’ll have some issues with whatever he’s building. Hell, I’m sure all those treehuggers in the state capitol would just love to hear about Stark cutting off the water supply of endangered species.”

“I’ll have Wade and the others keep an eye on this,” Lilia assured her, gesturing vaguely to the construction.

“Good idea,” Agatha agreed.

They rode back to the main house in silence. If it wasn’t one thing, it really was another. Evanora’s suit was still going, and now Stark was doing something sleezy, probably to try and get her to sell out, yet again. Sometimes Agatha thought it would be easier just to sell this place, but there was a stubborn part of her that refused to even entertain that thought. Her mother wouldn’t win. Stark wouldn’t win. She would protect this place, keep it safe for the next generation after her.

“Who’s that with Ollie?” Lilia asked.

Agatha, who had closed her eyes to relax for just a few moments, raised her head and followed Lilia’s gaze across the yard. Ollie was standing outside his chicken coop, pointing to the birds inside, and crouched down beside him was a girl. At first glance Agatha thought it was Nicky, but then she realized that the girl’s hair was darker, and she was wearing clothes that Nicky would never put on in a million years.

“Fucking kids,” Agatha muttered, jumping out of the side-by-side as soon as Lilia came to a stop. “Hey!”

Ollie turned as soon as he heard her voice. “Mama!” He ran toward her and grabbed her sleeve. “Come meet Tori, she’s my new sister.”

“What?” Agatha asked.

“Nicky and I tried to explain that just because I’m the same age as his sister doesn’t mean that I’m his sister, but he didn’t get it,” the girl said. “I’m Tori, Nicky’s friend. It’s nice to meet you, Ms. Harkness.”

“Oh,” Agatha said. “Sorry, Nicky didn’t tell me she was having anyone over. And please, call me Agatha.”

“Okay,” Tori said with a wide smile. There was something about the girl that was nagging Agatha, like she’d seen her before, but she couldn’t quite place where or when.

Nicky came up from the barn, leading Scratchy behind her. “There you are! I told you Ollie would drag you to see his chickens if you gave him half a chance.”

Tori shrugged. “I don’t mind. They’re pretty neat.”

“I invited Tori to ride a little bit before we work on homework, Mama, but I was looking for you or Lilia to ask who needed a workout,” Nicky told them.

“River needs to be worked today,” Lilia replied. “And it would be good to work that young stud around a mare before the weekend, make sure he’s gonna mind his manners.”

“Do you have any horse experience?” Agatha asked.

Tori nodded. “My grandpa trains horses. I have a mare of my own at home that I’ve raced a couple of times.”

“She should be able to handle her,” Lilia said.

“Alright, let me help you saddle her up,” Agatha told the girl. She looked at Nicky. “You go lunge Scratchy, let him get some energy out before you get in the saddle.”

“Yes, Mama,” Nicky replied, rolling her eyes.

Agatha led the teenager to the barn, watching her out of the corner of her eye as she went. She didn’t look like the kids Nicky normally hung out with, but Agatha thought that might actually be a good thing. Like most teenagers, Nicky wasn’t the most forthcoming about her social life, but Agatha thought the girls who made up Nicky’s usual circle of friends were, frankly, stuck up little bitches. Agatha hoped this girl, Tori, might be different.

“This is River,” Agatha said, gesturing to the red mare in the stall. “She’s normally my mount, and she can be a little… touchy.”

Tori peered into the stall. “She’s a red mare. Of course she’s touchy.”

Agatha chuckled. “You’re not wrong. There’s some treats over there, why don’t you bribe her while I go grab her tack?”

“Yes, ma’am,” Tori nodded.

Agatha smirked and went to the tackroom. Normally she put River in a saddle made for slower, long-distance riding, because on the ranch that was what she was more likely to do. But in the corner of the room, well-kept but covered with a fine layer of dust, was Agatha’s old barrel racing saddle and bit. She hadn’t raced in almost a decade, since before Ollie was born, but she had never sold her equipment, and Willow might be out of shape, but she would enjoy the challenge.

Agatha wiped down the saddle and carried it out. Tori had River eating out of the palm of her hand, literally, a wide smile on her face as she did so.

“No ears pinned back or anything,” Agatha noted. “Has she tried to bite you yet?”

“No,” Tori replied, laughing as the mare nosed at the bag of treats in her hand.

“Alright, you old nag, let’s see if you still have some speed left in you,” Agatha said, opening the stall door. They lead Willow to the crossties and gave her a quick grooming before Agatha started saddling her.

“Whoa,” Tori said, running her fingers over the embossed leather. “It’s so pretty.”

“You like it?” Agatha asked. The saddle was mostly brown leather with silver embellishments, but there were feathers carved into the skirt and fender that were painted purple, and the seat was custom made with purple suede as well.

“Purple’s kind of my favorite,” Tori told her.

“I never would’ve guessed,” Agatha deadpanned, looking pointedly at the purple streak in the girl’s hair. “C’mon, let’s go see if Nicky has worn out that young stallion yet.”

They went to the outdoor arena where three barrels were already set up. Lilia was leaning over the metal fencing, watching as Nicky did a slow lope through the pattern.

“Don’t forget the lead change as you bring him around the first barrel!” Agatha shouted.

“I’m just warming him up!” Nicky shouted back.

“You gotta do it in the warm up, too!” Agatha sighed. “I swear, she already thinks she knows everything.”

“Do you race?” Tori asked.

“I used to, but I had to stop a few years after Ollie was born,” Agatha replied. She pulled her hair to the side to reveal the scar on the back of her neck. “Took a nasty fall and cracked two vertebrae. I was almost paralyzed. Too much of a risk to do it now.” She looked from the teen to the horse she was leading. “You need a leg up?”

“That would be great,” Tori replied.

Agatha helped the teenager into the saddle, then adjusted the stirrup length. The girl looked right at home atop River, and she beamed down at Agatha.

“She knows what to do, but you’ll have to push her to get some speed,” Agatha told her, opening the fence. “Give her a few laps around the fenceline to warm up.”

“Yes, ma’am,” Tori nodded, giving Willow a squeeze to get her moving.

Nicky whooped and hollered as her friend entered the arena, and Agatha grinned at her daughter’s enthusiasm. She climbed up onto the fence beside Lilia and watched as Tori walked River around the arena a couple of times before pushing her into a trot.

“Looks like the kid knows what she’s doing,” Lilia noted.

“She’s got the basics down at least,” Agatha noted, looking back at Nicky. “For the love of— Nicky! Lead change!”

“I saw that eyeroll from here,” Lilia chuckled.

“Got a stallion and now she thinks she knows everything,” Agatha muttered.

“She thought that before she got the stallion,” Lilia told her. “She’s your daughter through and through, Agatha, there’s no denying that.”

A few minutes later, Nicky paused in her circuits around the barrels and rode over to where Tori was loping laps around the fenceline. Agatha watched the horses, but the paint did nothing more than sniff the mare. A moment later Nicky came trotting toward where they stood on the fence and Tori went toward the starting point for the barrel pattern.

“I told Tori to take a few turns,” Nicky said, stopping beside them. “Do you have a stopwatch? I wanna do a run.”

“You don’t need to run for practice,” Agatha reminded her.

“Just one time, me on Scratchy and Tori on River, once she’s got her bearings,” Nicky argued. “I just wanna see what she can do.”

“One run, after she’s warmed up,” Agatha agreed.

“Yes!” Nicky said with a victorious fist pump.

Agatha rolled her eyes at her daughter and looked back at where Tori was taking the cloverleaf pattern at a trot.

“Tighten her up around the barrels, she can do it,” Agatha called, and Tori nodded. On her next go-around she sped up to a lope and took River closer to the barrels. Agatha looked at her daughter. “You see how she actually listens when someone gives her constructive feedback? And how she’s changing leads around the first barrel?”

Nicky rolled her eyes again. For a moment Agatha wondered if her face could get stuck like that permanently, but she figured if that was possible her own eyes would’ve frozen there as a teenager. Lilia was unfortunately correct when she said that Nicky inherited her attitude straight from Agatha herself.

“Relax your hands!” Agatha shouted. “There you go, now bring her around a little further… That’s it.”

A few minutes later, Tori trotted River over toward them, a broad smile on her face. “How was that?”

“Good,” Agatha replied. “How do you feel on River?”

“She’s nice,” Tori replied, reaching down and scratching the mare’s neck. “She doesn’t take nearly as much push as my horse, which is nice, but I think Luna might have some speed on her. She’s one-quarter thoroughbred, so she has longer legs.”

“Do you race her?” Agatha asked.

“I raced her a couple of times last summer, when mom and I were visiting,” Tori answered. “I was hoping mom would coach me so I could enter more races now that we’ve moved, but she’s pretty busy with work.”

“Could Tori bring Luna over sometime?” Nicky asked.

“As long as she’s up to date on all her vaccines and dewormer, I don’t see why not,” Agatha replied.

“And you’d coach me?” Tori asked, her face lighting up with excitement.

“I can give you some pointers,” Agatha agreed.

“That would be awesome,” Tori said, looking at Nicky with a grin. “I can help you with pre-calc, and your mom can help me with barrel racing.”

Agatha chuckled. “Sounds like a good trade-off.”

Tori nodded in agreement.

“Can we race now?” Nicky asked, nearly vibrating with excitement.

“Full speed?” Tori asked.

“Yep,” Nicky replied. “I’ll even go first, to give you a break.”

“Oh, so generous,” Tori smirked.

“Are you timing, Mama?”

“I’ve got it,” Lilia replied, pulling a stopwatch from her pocket.

“Did you just have that?” Agatha asked under her breath.

“I had a feeling I might need it,” LIlia shrugged. “Call it intuition.”

Nicky walked Scratchy into position, and the stallion seemed to understand that this run was different. He tugged against the bit in excitement, feeding off his rider, but he never once did anything that Agatha worried might put her daughter in danger. Once they were in position, Nicky kicked him into high gear, and the paint took off.

“She did the lead change,” Lilia commented as Nicky rounded the first barrel.

“Yeah, but she should’ve taken him further around before cueing it,” Agatha replied. “Now he’s going too wide, that’ll lose time.”

The stallion was fast, that was for sure, but there were plenty of small things that Nicky could improve on to make his run faster. They rounded the last barrel and Nicky pulled him in so tight, trying to make up for lost time, that she nearly came out of the saddle.

“Stay in your fucking seat!” Agatha shouted. She watched as Nicky kicked wildly on the final stretch, trying to make up for time. “For fuck’s sake.”

“How’d I do?” Nicky asked, catching her breath as she led Scratchy over to them.

“16.35 seconds,” Lilia told her.

Nicky beamed. “I never got under 16.5 on Bullseye.”

“You could get under sixteen with Scratchy if you’d focus,” Agatha told her. “Maybe even fifteen.”

Nicky’s victorious face turned to a frown. “We’ll get there.”

Lilia cleared her throat. “Tori, your turn.”

“Woohoo! Let’s go!” Nicky cheered as Tori trotted into position.

Agatha watched as Tori gave River a kick to get her going and the mare took off like a shot. They were tight around the first barrel where Nicky had been wide, but nearly toppled the second. Tori stayed in the seat, a bit wide on the final barrel as well, but once they were in the home stretch River knew exactly what to do, and the little red mare poured on the speed.

Beside her, Lilia started laughing, and Agatha didn’t even have to ask what the time was. Tori trotted over, an expectant look on her face.

“15.993,” Lilia declared.

“Holy shit!” Nicky shouted.

“I think that’s the fastest that mare’s run in years,” Lilia said between guffaws.

“You’ve got to enter some races,” Nicky said. “I’m going to a jackpot with Scratchy next weekend. Do you wanna go with us?”

“I should probably practice with Luna before then,” Tori said. “Not that Willow isn’t great, but I’d want to ride on my own horse, you know?”

“Of course,” Agatha nodded. “But Nicky’s right, you’re very good.”

“I don’t know if mom is working next weekend or not,” Tori told them. “She might not be able to take me.”

“We’ve got room in the trailer, if you want,” Agatha offered. “I don’t mind.”

“You should come over the night before!” Nicky exclaimed. “We can have a sleepover! Can we, mama? Please?”

Agatha couldn’t remember the last time she had seen her daughter this excited. “If Tori’s parents say it’s okay, then I don’t see why not.”

“Yes!” Nicky exclaimed. “Say yes, Tori, please?”

“Sure, yeah,” Tori agreed, a small smile on her face.

“Sounds like a plan,” Agatha said. “Now, didn’t you two say something about pre-calculus homework?”

Nicky groaned. “Ugh… yes.”

“Get these horses put away and fed and get to it then,” Agatha ordered.

The girls trotted away side-by-side, laughing as they went. Agatha watched them go, that niggling feeling returning to the back of her mind.

“That girl’s good,” Lilia commented. “Reminds me of you when you were younger.”

“Nicky?” Agatha asked.

“Well, obviously Nicky reminds me of you,” Lilia said. “I was referring to the other one. Tori.”

“How so?” Agatha asked.

“Lots of things,” Lilia said. “Who are her people?”

“I don’t know, she didn’t say,” Agatha replied. “I’ll ask Nicky later. For now I’m just glad she’s making new friends, and that this friend seems like an improvement over the Stark girl.”

“Amen to that,” Lilia agreed. “Speaking of Stark, you gonna make those phone calls?”

Agatha had almost forgotten. “Ah fuck.”

Over the next two weeks, Tori became a fixture at the ranch. She was there every day after school, even on days she wasn’t helping Nicky with her pre-calculus homework. Some days she helped Nicky with her highland calves, some days she and Nicky spent helping Ollie collect and wash chicken eggs. One day Agatha walked into the kitchen to find Remy teaching them how to play poker at the table, dinner forgotten on the stove.

Nicky had had friends before, but Agatha had never seen her take to another person quite like this. Agatha had even questioned if it was romantic, but Nicky had assured her that she was one-hundred percent straight, and that while Tori was into girls, she wasn’t into Nicky. They were just good friends, like Agatha and Jen, and Agatha was grateful that Nicky had found a friend like that, especially since her previous friendship with the Stark girl and her circle seemed to have fallen apart.

That was probably a good thing, because Jen had dug into Stark’s building permits and found that he was planning to dam the river to create a reservoir for an AI data center he wanted to build. Jen had managed to put a stop to it for now, calling in several environmental groups to do so, but it would probably be a drawn-out process.

The Friday before the jackpot race, Nicky and Tori took a small trailer to pick up Tori’s black mare. She brought the mare over three days a week for Agatha to coach her, and Agatha enjoyed their sessions immensely. It also helped that when Nicky saw how much Tori was improving from listening to Agatha’s feedback, she started listening to her mother as well. Agatha thought it was a win-win for all of them. After they finished a last bit of training and had packed the trailer for the next morning, the girls retreated to Nicky’s bedroom for their sleepover. Agatha could hear the sound of the girls laughing even through the thick log walls, and even though she could only imagine the shape they would be in for the race, she couldn’t bring herself to go make them sleep. There were some moments in life that were simply part of growing up, and staying up too late at a sleepover with your best friend was definitely one of those moments.

Saturday morning came bright and early, and sure enough both girls trudged down to the breakfast table with dark circles under their eyes and bedhead. Agatha smirked over her coffee as they collapsed into their seats. If she didn’t have the liquor locked away she might think they were hungover, but she knew better. This was simply the result of copious amounts of sugar and laughter the night before and a lack of sleep.

“You guys look awful,” Ollie said, looking at them with wide eyes. “Are you sick?”

“No,” they both said at the same time. Agatha chuckled.

“So how many horror movies did you watch?” she asked.

“We started watching the original Friday the 13th, but then Ollie knocked on the door, so we watched The Princess Bride instead,” Nicky replied. “He went to bed halfway through, but we watched the rest anyway.”

“Ollie, I told you not to bother your sister last night,” Agatha chastised. She turned to the girls. “You could’ve just told him to leave. It was your sleepover.”

Tori shrugged. “He’s cool. And I had never watched The Princess Bride anyway.”

“Never?” Agatha asked. “That’s one of our favorites around here.”

“I liked it,” Tori told her. “I didn’t watch anything with princesses growing up. I’d throw a tantrum anytime my mom tried to put on a Disney movie. But I was obsessed with the Land Before Time movies.”

“Also classics,” Agatha agreed.

Remy served them a breakfast of pancakes with eggs and bacon, and both girls consumed an obscene amount of food in that way that only active, growing teenagers could. Once they were finished, they headed upstairs to get ready for the race. Agatha helped Ollie get dressed and then dressed herself, and by that time they were running behind.

“Girls, are you dressed?” Agatha called, knocking on Nicky’s bedroom door.

“We’re almost ready.” Nicky shouted back.

Agatha opened the door to see Nicky standing over Tori, a tube of mascara in hand. Agatha got the impression that Tori rarely wore makeup except heavy eyeliner, so the sight of Nicky styling her with her more feminine, understated style was definitely a change. Nicky stood back with a flourish, looking at her friend with a smirk.

“There we go!” Nicky declared. “You look very bonita.”

Tori was wearing a purple and white plaid button up, jeans, and cowboy boots. Nicky also wore a button up but hers was seafoam green and white stripes, jeans, and her boots. They both had their hair down, Nicky’s in carefully-curled waves, Tori’s in natural soft waves that frizzed slightly at the ends. They had their differences, but standing side by side, Agatha could almost believe they were sisters, they were so similar.

She shook her head at the thought.

“You both look great, now let’s go! Vamanos!” Agatha said, hustling them up and out.

The race was an hour and a half drive away, in a little town outside of Bozeman. Agatha sent the girls to register while she unloaded the horses. Ollie sat on the tailgate watching, clearly deep in thought.

“Mama?”

“Yes, Ollie?” she said, her voice echoing slightly as she backed Scratchy out of the trailer.

“You and I have blue eyes.”

Agatha looked up, curious where this line of thinking was going. “Yes, we do.”

“And Nicky has brown eyes.”

“Yes, she does.”

“Why doesn’t Nicky have blue eyes like us?” he asked.

“Well, Nicky’s other mother had brown eyes,” Agatha told him. “Nicky has brown eyes like her.”

“Oh,” Ollie said, his face pinched with thought. He was quiet for a long time, and Agatha finished tying Scratchy to the side of the trailer. She went back inside for Luna, taking the mare around to tie her on the opposite side of the trailer.

“Tori has blue eyes,” Ollie said after a while.

“What?” Agatha said, confused by his statement.

“Tori has blue eyes,” Ollie repeated, hopping off the tailgate. “I’m hungry. Did you bring any snacks?”

“Yeah, hon, they’re in the bag behind the driver’s seat,” Agatha told him.

Nicky and Tori returned from registration and they quickly set to work grooming the horses, both quiet and focused now that they were at the event. Agatha watched them both, offering help when needed, but they were both well versed in this process. Nicky swung up onto Scratchy first, and Tori used the wheel well of the trailer to boost herself up onto Luna.

“Give them a little walk around to warm them up, and I’ll see you girls at the arena, alright?” Agatha said, giving each horse a quick pat. “C’mon, Ollie, let’s go find a seat.”

At a small jackpot event like this there weren’t always seats, but this one was held in a slightly more used arena, so there were metal bleachers on each side. Agatha and Ollie climbed to the topmost level and sat, squinting against the bright sun.

“There they are!” Ollie exclaimed, pointing to where Tori and Nicky were waiting at the edge of the arena along with the other riders.

Agatha could feel her nerves climbing with every successive run before the girls. It was a 4D race, which meant more chances at possibly winning a cash prize of some sort, but Agatha didn’t care if either of them won, not really. But she knew that the girls would care, and she didn’t want either of them going home disappointed, even if she knew that was part of competing and growing up. She supposed she should’ve been rooting for Nicky more than Tori, but she found herself just as anxious for the other girl as she was for her own daughter.

“Tori’s next!” Ollie shouted, standing on the bleacher. Agatha grabbed hold of his belt, just in case he got excited and bolted like he did when he was younger, and her other hand clenched her knee so tightly that her knuckles turned white.

“The next racer up is Victoria Vidal on Luna!” the announcer called, his voice booming over the rattling speakers.

It was as if the ground fell out from beneath Agatha’s feet. The sound of the small crowd of people faded away, overtaken by the sound of Agatha’s own heartbeat, and the echo of the announcer’s voice still ringing in her ears.

Victoria Vidal.

Tori.

Vidal.

Puzzle pieces suddenly began sliding into place in Agatha’s mind. That nagging feeling she got whenever Tori was around, that sense of familiarity, suddenly made sense. It seemed so obvious in retrospect that Agatha felt like an absolute fucking idiot.

Tori was Rio’s daughter. She had to be. It wasn’t like Westview was crawling with people with Vidal as their surname. Plus she looked just like Rio, except for her eyes.

Tori has blue eyes.

Rio had a daughter. A daughter the same age as Nicky. A daughter with blue eyes.

“Mama, let me go!” Ollie demanded, yanking away from Agatha’s hold on his belt.

Agatha looked up, reality crashing back in on her. She wasn’t sure how much time had passed, but she could see a brown and white horse tail trotting out of the arena. While she was in the middle of her revelation, she had apparently missed both Tori and Nicky’s runs.

“Fuck,” Agatha muttered, letting go of Ollie’s belt. He adjusted his pants before turning and looking at her.

“Mama, that’s a bad word.”

“I know. Sorry,” Agatha stuttered. “C’mon, let’s go see your sister.”

Sisters, said the voice in Agatha’s mind, and she wished it would shut up.

“But what about the other riders?” Ollie asked.

“Ollie, come on,” Agatha ordered.

They left the stands and Agatha marched toward the trucks and trailers. People and horses moved out of her way, and she even pushed one man who wasn’t moving fast enough. She was just rounding the corner toward the truck when she heard Nicky and Tori laughing, and the sound stopped her in her tracks.

What was she doing? She couldn’t confront Tori about this, not now, she’d look like a crazy person. And it seemed like Tori might be just as in the dark about the other half of her parentage as Nicky was.

Agatha, on the other hand, was absolutely certain that Tori was her daughter. Sure, it was possible that Rio had moved on quickly after they broke up and got pregnant with someone else, but looking at Tori, and looking at her beside Nicky, it was clear as day. Hell, she had even thought it earlier that morning, before she knew Tori’s last name.

Sisters.

Being sure of that fact didn’t mean Agatha knew what to do with the information. She couldn’t tell the girls, no, that was out of the question. She needed to talk to Rio, to ask her why on earth she had kept Tori a secret from her. But that opened up the door for Rio to find out about Nicky, and she would have just as many questions. Agatha felt like her chest was splitting open as she considered her options, as the emotions hit her one by one.

She had a daughter. A daughter that she knew nothing about. A daughter that Rio had kept secret from her for over seventeen years. The betrayal and anger that Agatha felt were like nothing she had ever known.

And yet, she had done the same thing to Rio.

Agatha didn’t have time to unpack all that. Instead she took a deep breath and schooled her features, boxing up her emotions and tucking them into a tiny box at the back of her brain to address later. She didn’t have to figure it all out right now, in fact, it was better if she didn’t. It wasn’t only her secret to tell. She needed time to make a plan, figure out the best way to approach Rio, if there even was a good way to have the conversation that they clearly needed to have.

But not today. Today she had two teenage girls who were none the wiser about their parentage who were simply celebrating successful runs on their horses. And Agatha wouldn’t ruin that for them.

She rounded the corner as Ollie ran up to the girls, greeting both of them with a high five.

“Did you see us, bud?” Nicky asked, reaching down to ruffle his hair.

“Yeah, you went super fast!” Ollie exclaimed. “You were fast, too, Tori!”

“Thanks, Ollie,” Tori said, ruffling his hair just like Nicky did. “Nicky had a little bit of an edge on me today, though.”

Agatha cleared her throat. “I missed your final times.”

“I got a 16.103, and Tori got 16.2,” Nicky told her.

“Amazing,” Agatha said, but she wasn’t talking about the numbers. She was staring at Tori, at the blue eyes that looked so much like her own. It was almost laughable, that Nicky had inherited Rio’s eyes so perfectly while Tori had Agatha’s.

“Mama, are you okay?” Nicky asked.

“Yeah,” Agatha nodded. “I will be.”

Agatha watched as the girls unsaddled and groomed their horses, working together instead of separating to each work on their own horse, as if they couldn’t stand to be more than a few feet apart.

They deserved the truth, Agatha thought. Even if it hurt her, even if it hurt Rio, their daughters deserved to know the truth. But it wasn’t just Agatha’s secret to tell.

She needed to talk to Rio.

Chapter 10: Rio

Chapter Summary

Rio gets called to the principal’s office and comes to a shocking realization

Monday was the absolute worst day of the week to be a vet. That wasn’t just Rio’s opinion, she had the facts to back it up. Mondays were always busy, with back-to-back appointments. Issues that had popped up over the weekend that weren’t urgent enough to warrant a house call or an actual emergency visit were all worked into the schedule. They never scheduled surgeries for Mondays for that reason, and Dr. McCoy tried to avoid house calls on Mondays unless it was urgent, specifically for that reason. Every single Monday felt like a marathon, except instead of pacing herself, Rio was running full sprint for the entire day.

So when her cell phone rang on Monday shortly after lunch— which consisted of a spoonful of peanut butter eaten between appointments— she didn’t answer. And when it rang again while she was removing porcupine quills from a labrador’s muzzle, she ignored it again. She was in the stable listening to a horse’s stomach for gut sounds when Rahne found her.

“Dr. Vidal? You have a phone call,” Rahne called.

Rio sighed. “Have them leave a message.”

“It’s Principal Davis,” Rahne told her. “She has Tori in her office, and apparently it’s urgent. They need you to come down to the school as soon as possible.”

Rio nearly dropped her stethoscope. “Shit.”

“Go, Doc,” Logan told her. “Hank and I can manage.”

“Thank you,” Rio said, hurrying out of the stall.

The drive to the school was short, but still long enough for Rio to imagine all sorts of terrible scenarios. Tori had never been called to the principal’s office for behavior, so Rio could only imagine there was some sort of emergency. She parked her truck in front of the school, not caring that it might block traffic for afternoon pickup, and rushed into the office.

“Wanda, what the hell happened?” Rio demanded. “Is Tori hurt? Is she okay?”

“Rio, calm down, Tori is fine,” Wanda assured her.

“Then why the hell did I have to drop everything and come here?” Rio asked.

“Let me just tell Mrs. Davis that you’re here,” Wanda said, standing and heading down the hall. Wanda poked her head into the principal’s office for a moment, then turned to Rio and beckoned her to come down.

Principal Davis was sitting behind her desk and a male teacher with graying temples stood behind her. Tori was on the sofa across from her, looking near panicked at being there, but to Rio’s surprise she wasn’t alone. Nicky sat on the sofa beside her, and where Tori looked panicked, Nicky just looked angry, a deep scowl set in her features.

“Mami!” Tori exclaimed when Rio walked in. “Mami, it’s not true, we didn’t do anything! This is all just a misunderstanding!”

“It’s a bunch of bullshit is what it is,” Nicky muttered.

“Language, Nicky,” Principal Davis interjected, but it was a half-hearted warning. Nicky just rolled her eyes in response.

“Mrs. Davis, what exactly is going on?” Rio asked. She looked at the man behind the desk. “Who are you?”

“This is Dr. Strange, Tori and Nicky’s pre-calculus teacher,” the principal replied. “It might be best to wait until Nicky’s mother gets here, so we can discuss this with both of you at the same—”

“Where the hell is my daughter?”

Rio’s stomach dropped. No, there was no way…

“Ms. Harkness— Agatha, please—”

Nicky’s scowl morphed into a smirk, and suddenly Rio knew exactly where she had seen that gleam in her eyes before. The only difference was that Agatha’s eyes were blue and Nicky’s were…

Brown.

Agatha stormed into the office like a human hurricane. Her hair was down in wild waves that fell to her waist, she wore a loose gray cardigan over a flowy floral dress, and boots. Her blue eyes scanned the room, taking measure of everyone there. She didn’t even acknowledge Rio’s presence, just turned to Principal Davis with an expectant expression.

“Well?”

“Ms. Harkness, Dr. Vidal, it has been brought to my attention that Nicky and Tori may have cheated on their most recent pre-calculus quizzes.”

“What?” Rio exclaimed.

“But we didn’t!” Tori argued.

“That’s bullshit,” Nicky huffed.

Agatha looked between all of them with a calculating gaze. “What proof do you have to back up these accusations?”

“Nicole’s test scores have been nothing short of abysmal for this entire semester,” Dr. Strange told them.

“Nicky,” Agatha corrected. “She goes by Nicky.”

“I prefer to call my students by their full names,” Dr. Strange told her.

“And I, her mother, am saying that you should use her preferred nickname,” Agatha replied.

“Agatha, perhaps we should stick to the issue at hand,” Principal Davis said.

Agatha looked at Nicky, who shrugged, before looking back at the teacher. “Fine.”

The man gave a smug grin and Rio had to fight the urge to roll her eyes. This guy was a prick, perhaps even worse than Tori had described.

“Nicole scored an 86 and a 93 on her most recent quizzes in my class,” Dr. Strange continued. “Such a rapid improvement was enough to raise my suspicions. Initially I thought that perhaps Victoria was an innocent bystander, and that Nicole had simply copied her answers from Victoria’s paper. But when I confronted Nicole, Victoria told me that she had been helping her. So it would seem that Victoria allowed Nicole to copy her answers on her quizzes to improve her grade.”

There was a moment of silence as soon as Dr. Strange finished his accusation. Rio glanced at the girls, who were both staring at their teacher with identical expressions of outrage.

Identical.

“Are you done?” Agatha asked, raising a brow at the man.

The smug look on his face faded slightly. “Yes, Mrs. Harkness.”

“Ms. Harkness,” Agatha corrected. “I think it’s very interesting that when Tori explained that she had been helping Nicky with her pre-calculus, your first instinct was to assume that the girls had worked together to cheat, Dr. Strange.”

“It seemed the most logical conclusion,” the man explained.

“Perhaps to you,” Agatha huffed. “Mrs. Hart—”

“It’s Davis, dear,” the principal reminded her.

“Oh, I thought we were using whatever name we preferred,” Agatha quipped. “Mrs. Davis, over the last two weeks, Tori has been coming to my house after school every day to help Nicky with her pre-calculus homework and tutor her on concepts that Mr. Strange—”

“Doctor,” the teacher corrected.

“That Mister Strange has failed to explain sufficiently,” Agatha concluded.

“I doubt that a sixteen-year-old’s tutelage could explain Nicole’s rapid improvement,” Dr. Strange scoffed.

“Based on the girls’ description of your lackluster performance as their teacher, I believe that it does,” Agatha argued.

“How dare you?” Dr. Strange exclaimed.

“How dare you accuse my daughter of cheating just because you’re a terrible teacher?”

“Alright, everyone, let’s take a breath,” Mrs. Davis interrupted, rubbing her temple like the entire situation was giving her a headache. “Dr. Vidal, has Tori been tutoring Nicky as Ms. Harkness says?”

“Oh, now you’re calling me a liar?” Agatha huffed, crossing her arms over her chest.

Mrs. Davis gave her a look that was very reminiscent of how she had looked at them as teenagers before her gaze went back to Rio. “Dr. Vidal?”

“Yes,” Rio replied. Not that she had realized exactly where Tori was going, a fact that she was kicking herself for now. She had never once asked Nicky’s surname, had never asked for her parents’ names. She had trusted the teenager because of what she saw during her internship, so she had given Tori permission to go to her home after school, had even given her permission to take her horse and go to the races the weekend before. She had no idea that Nicky was Agatha’s daughter.

Agatha’s daughter.

“Dr. Strange, please step out for a moment and close the door,” Principal Davis instructed.

Dr. Strange balked. “Mrs. Davis, I hardly think—”

“Just for a moment, please,” Mrs. Davis said, her smile saccharine sweet but leaving no room for argument.

Dr. Strange huffed as he stepped outside.

“And close the door, Stephen,” the principal repeated.

As soon as the door was shut, Mrs. Davis leaned back in her chair and rubbed her temples. “I swear, that man—”

“Arrogant prick,” Agatha muttered.

Mrs. Davis opened her eyes and looked between Agatha and Rio. “Well, this is certainly bringing back memories. Not the first time you two have been in this office together, is it?”

Rio could feel her cheeks flushing. Beside her Agatha stood a bit straighter, tossing her hair haughtily.

“I had hoped that your daughters wouldn’t be as much trouble as you two,” Mrs. Davis continued.

Your daughters. Rio didn’t dare look toward the girls, because she knew that as soon as she did, her mind would finish putting together the puzzle she was desperately denying for the moment.

“Our daughters didn’t do anything wrong,” Agatha said, and Rio’s stomach did a strange flip at the way she said it. There was no way…

“I believe you,” Mrs. Davis replied. “I cannot speak blatantly about a teacher’s effectiveness to parents, of course, but just know that I am aware of some issues in Dr. Strange’s classes and we’re working to address them.”

“Really?” Agatha said, her voice thick with disbelief.

“Really,” Mrs. Davis replied. “As for the issue at hand, I am going to ask one of our other math instructors to create a short quiz that covers the concepts from the last two units covered in class. Nicky will take that quiz tomorrow, with me, so that there can be no suspicion of cheating.”

“Hardly seems fair since she didn’t cheat in the first place,” Agatha scoffed.

“It’s okay, Mama,” Nicky assured her. “I’ll pass it, no problem.”

“What about Tori?” Rio asked.

“Once Nicky’s name is cleared, by extension Tori’s will be as well,” Mrs. Davis replied. She looked from the adults to where the girls were sitting. “I want to say, girls, that I do believe you. This quiz, Nicky, is just a formality so there is no doubt. And I want to commend you, Nicky, for putting in the extra time and work outside of class to improve your work, and you, Tori, for helping her. It shows true character on both your parts.”

Both girls looked pleased with the praise. Rio could see why Mrs. Davis had become a principal.

“Ms. Harkness, Dr. Vidal, would you like to take the girls home now, or have them return to class until dismissal?” Mrs. Davis asked.

“Please don’t make us go back to gym,” Nicky groaned.

“With that reaction, you’re definitely going back,” Agatha replied.

Nicky groaned again before standing. “Fine. C’mon, Tori.”

“Do I have to?” Tori looked at Rio with a pout that was far too reminiscent of Agatha Harkness.

“Dr. Vidal, make her stay,” Nicky pleaded. “We’re playing dodgeball. She can’t abandon me now.”

Rio shrugged. “A little dodgeball never killed anyone.”

“Pretty sure it did,” Tori grumbled, but she followed Nicky out of the office anyway.

“Those two have become like two peas in a pod,” Mrs. Davis chuckled. “If I didn’t know any better, I would think they were sisters.”

Rio felt like there was a stone in her gut. Beside her Agatha cleared her throat.

“Well, if we’re done here, I have an appointment with my attorney,” she announced. “Mrs. Davis, I’d say it was a pleasure, but that would be a lie.”

“The feeling is mutual, Agatha, dear,” Mrs. Davis replied.

Before Rio could blink, Agatha hurried from the office. Rio watched her go, her mind still spinning as she finally allowed the realization to hit her.

Nicky was Agatha’s daughter. Agatha’s daughter, who was the same age as Tori. Agatha’s daughter who had brown eyes the exact same color as Rio’s.

“I, uh, I have to go,” Rio said, giving Mrs. Davis an awkward wave before running out of the office.

She thought she heard the woman chuckle as she left.

“Dr. Vidal? Is everything okay?” Wanda called as she ran past, but Rio ignored her.

She ran out of the office and looked around frantically. Agatha was already in the parking lot, unlocking the door on a sleek black sedan that probably cost more than Rio made in a year.

“Agatha!” Rio shouted. Agatha shuddered like she was startled, but she didn’t stop, didn’t even look toward Rio. Rio ran across the drive, to the parking lot, and finally stood in front of Agatha’s car. “Agatha, wait!”

“I have an appointment,” Agatha said angrily, but her voice was muffled. She wiped at her eyes and Rio realized she was crying.

“When were you going to tell me?” Rio demanded.

“Tell you what?” Agatha asked.

“About Nicky,” Rio said, stepping closer. “You weren’t, were you?”

“Rio, I don’t know what you’re—”

Rio grabbed the car door before Agatha could sit down in the seat. When Agatha looked up, her face was mere inches away from Rio’s.

“When were you going to tell me about my daughter?” Rio asked, her voice low.

Agatha let go of the door and stepped back, like she was desperate to put distance between them. Rio expected her to look upset, or perhaps guilty at being caught. Instead, she looked furious, perhaps even more angry than Rio.

“When were you going to tell me about Tori?” Agatha asked.

“Don’t you fucking dare try and turn this around on me,” Rio growled.

“Typical Rio, so high and mighty, acting like you’re so much better than everyone else,” Agatha scoffed. “But don’t you dare get angry at me when you did the exact same thing.”

“Like you didn’t know,” Rio huffed. “Seventeen years, and you never told me about Nicky. Seventeen years and you never asked about Tori.”

The anger in Agatha’s expression shifted, overtaken by confusion. “Why the fuck would I ask about her?”

“I guess you assumed that I went through with it,” Rio said, shaking her head. “But I didn’t. I made it work. I struggled, but I kept her, and I raised her all on my own. So don’t you dare think that you’re going to have anything to do with her now, after all this time.”

Agatha’s face hardened, her emotionless mask coming down. “We’ll see about that.”

She stepped closer again, and Rio automatically stepped back. Agatha got into the car without another word, slammed the door behind her, and tore out of the parking space, almost running over Rio’s foot in the process. Rio watched her go, heart pounding so loud that she could hear the whooshing of the blood in her ears. She wanted to drive after her, wanted to yank her out of the car and force her to continue the conversation. She wanted to grab Agatha by the shoulders and shake her, she wanted to slap her.

Part of her wanted to kiss her, but Rio shoved that thought deep down, suffocating it beneath seventeen years of betrayal and heartache.

“Fuck!” Rio shouted at the top of her lungs, kicking the tire of the closest car so hard that pain reverberated through her foot. “Fuck!”

She stomped across the parking lot to her truck and climbed into the driver’s seat, slamming the door angrily. Once she was closed up in the cab of the truck, Rio screamed and hit the steering wheel over and over again until her hands ached. Finally her throat felt raw, and her cheeks burned from the tears running down them.

She wasn’t sure what she expected, but somehow it wasn’t… that.

Seventeen years ago, she thought that Agatha rejecting her and their unborn child was the worst feeling in the world. But she had survived, and what's more, she and Tori had thrived, without Agatha in their lives. To now find out that on top of ignoring her and Tori for all this time, Agatha had another child and kept her from Rio?

Rio’s heart was in pieces.

Rio waited in the truck until dismissal, gradually pulling herself together as more cars lined up behind her. She had no idea what she was going to do moving forward, but she knew that she didn’t want Tori going to Agatha’s house again. So she waited until she saw her daughter come out of the building to the dismissal area.

Tori wasn’t alone.

Rio should’ve expected it. Tori and Nicky had become near inseparable over the last two weeks, and until now she had been grateful for it. But now, knowing what she did…

Rio thought her heart couldn’t break any further, but she felt another piece shatter inside her.

She opened the door and stood on the running board, waving and whistling to get Tori’s attention. Tori looked confused to see her at first, but then she headed over. Nicky, unfortunately, followed.

“Mami? What are you doing here?” Tori asked.

“I thought I’d just hang around and pick you up,” Rio told her, forcing a smile onto her face.

“Oh,” Tori replied, still confused. “I was planning to go over to Nicky’s. Is that okay?”

“I’ll bring her home as soon as we finish our homework, Dr. Vidal,” Nicky assured her.

Rio clenched her fist so hard that her short nails dug into her palm. “Not today, girls.”

Both girls’ faces fell. Tori looked at Nicky, who shrugged. “Maybe another day, then.”

“Sure,” Rio lied.

“See you tomorrow,” Nicky said, bumping Tori’s shoulder. “See you in the morning, Dr. Vidal!”

“Yep!” Rio called back, her voice cracking.

Tori was still frowning as she got into the passenger’s seat. “Mami? What’s going on?”

“Nothing,” Rio told her. “I just think, after what happened today, that maybe you shouldn’t be spending so much time with Nicky and her mother.”

“What?” Tori exclaimed. “But that’s not fair! We didn’t even do anything.”

“That’s not entirely true though, is it?” Rio challenged.

“Is this because they’re Harknesses?” Tori demanded.

“I told you that I didn’t want you hanging around them,” Rio replied.

“But then you gave me permission to hang out with Nicky!” Tori argued.

“That was only because I didn’t know her last name at the time,” Rio explained. “But you did, and you still went against my explicit instructions.”

“Your instructions were not explicit, they were actually very confusing,” Tori told her.

“Then you ask for clarification,” Rio chastised. “You’re a smart kid, Tori. You knew that if you asked for clarification, if I knew Nicky’s last name, then I wouldn’t let you two spend time together. So instead, you did what you wanted. Isn’t that so?”

Tori didn’t reply. She sat back in her seat and crossed her arms over her chest, and by god did she look like Agatha when she did that. “This isn’t fair. Nicky and I haven’t done anything. You like Nicky, for fuck’s sake.”

“Language, Tori,” Rio warned. “And how I feel about Nicky doesn’t matter. You deliberately disobeyed me.”

“I did not!” Tori argued. She looked down at her lap for a long minute before finally looking back at Rio. “Is this about Nicky’s mom?”

“Of course not,” Rio said, but she answered too quickly.

“It is, isn’t it?” Tori asked. “You know Agatha, don’t you?”

“That’s none of your concern,” Rio growled.

“The way Principal Davis was talking… You two went to school together, didn’t you? Did Agatha get you into trouble, Mami? Is that what you’re worried about? You think Nicky will get me into trouble?”

“Something like that,” Rio muttered.

“Mami, we’re not doing anything bad!” Tori claimed. “We’re just really good friends. And Agatha, she’s really nice. She’s been teaching me about barrel racing and cattle ranching. She’s great, Mami. You’d really like her if you’d just—”

“That’s enough!” Rio shouted, her voice reverberating in the cab of the truck. She didn’t need to hear her daughter singing the praises of the woman who had abandoned them before she was even born.

Tori stared at her with wide, frightened eyes. Rio could count on one hand the number of times she had raised her voice at her daughter. After her own childhood, she made a point not to. But here she was, losing her cool, and all because of Agatha Harkness.

Rio took a deep breath, trying to calm herself. “This is not up for discussion, Tori. I don’t want you spending time with Nicky until further notice.”

“That’s not fair!” Tori argued.

“Maybe not, but I’m your mother, and that’s just how it’s going to be,” Rio told her. “I’ll call the school tomorrow and have you switched to riding the bus home until we can see about getting your license and a car for you.”

Tori slumped further down in her seat and turned to look out the window. “I hate you.”
