Agatha smirked as she drove up the drive. When she parked her car, she saw Tori sitting on the front porch alone.

“Howdy, stranger,” Agatha greeted, leaning against the porch railing. “You out here by yourself?”

“Yeah, Nicky’s working on biology homework and Ollie’s playing some computer game,” Tori replied. “Mami’s still at work and I’m just… bored.”

“Uh-oh, don’t say that,” Agatha warned. “Never say you’re bored if you live on a ranch, kiddo. Somebody’ll find a chore for you to do.”

“I already mucked stalls until Lilia told me to clear out,” Tori told her. “She said you pay people to do that.”

“Lilia’s getting soft in her old age. When I was a kid she had me working my ass off,” Agatha recalled. “Of course, if I wasn’t working I was getting in trouble, so maybe she had ulterior motives. She knows you’re a good kid, so she doesn’t have to push you as hard.”

“Lilia worked here when you were a kid?” Tori asked.

“Oh, yeah, that old broad practically raised me,” Agatha told her. She looked Tori up and down. “You wanna go for a ride? Just the two of us?”

“Really?” Tori asked, her face lighting up with excitement.

“Sure,” Agatha nodded. “Think you can get the horses saddled while I change?”

“Yeah, I can do that,” Tori agreed, standing and hurrying toward the barn. Halfway down the drive she turned back around and shouted. “Where are we going?”

Agatha didn’t answer, but she knew exactly where she wanted to take Tori. An hour later they were on horseback, meandering up the side of a mountain. It was a treacherous trail, but River and Luna were sure-footed and navigated the rocks and pines with ease.

“Where are we going exactly?” Tori asked.

Agatha chuckled. “You’ll see.”

After another half-hour of riding, they came to their destination. The trees seemed to open up, and a few feet ahead of them the mountain dropped off in a steep cliff face. Agatha took Tori’s reins in her hand and carefully led her horse close to the edge. From there, they could look out over almost the entirety of the ranch.

“Oh wow,” Tori said, her voice thick with awe. “This is— Holy shit.”

“I told you it was worth the ride,” Agatha told her.

“You can see the house from here,” Tori said, pointing.

“Mmhmm, and over there’s Lilia’s cabin. If you follow the river you can see the south pastures where the cattle are all grazing now. And over there’s pasture five with the open mares.”

Tori smirked. “It’s giving Lion King.”

Agatha looked at her with confusion. “Huh?”

“You know… Everything the light touches is part of our kingdom? That part of The Lion King?”

“Oh,” Agatha chuckled. “I suppose it does.”

“How far does it go?” Tori asked.

“The ranch itself is just over thirty-four thousand acres,” Agatha told her.

“I have no idea how big that is,” Tori replied honestly.

“Too big for us to see all of it today,” Agatha said. “Come on. There’s more I want to show you.”

“There’s more?”

The ride back down the mountain was even more difficult than going up, but they made it safely. Once they were on more level ground, Agatha led Tori through the trees and hills, to a small grove. The remains of a log cabin took up most of the grove, a rectangular stone foundation and a few decaying logs and wooden shingles.

“Is this a real log cabin? Like, from settler days?” Tori asked.

“It is, and it’s more than that,” Agatha told her. “This is where your four-times great-grandfather Hiram Harkness built his cabin when he first settled this property over one hundred years ago. He came here with his wife, Agnes, and their three children, Nicholas, Henry, and Emma.”

“His son’s name was Nicholas?” Tori asked.

Agatha grinned. “I named Nicky after him. He took over the property when Hiram got older, and he was the one who really started turning this place into what it is today. Of course, it took several more generations. But this is where it all started.”

“So Hiram was my great-great-great-great grandfather,” Tori said, counting on her fingers as she said it. “And then Nicholas was my great-great-great grandfather…”

Agatha chuckled. “Come on.”

They rode a little past the grove, through the trees, until it opened up onto a clearing. From this spot they could see the river as it wound through the grassy hills, and in the distance they could just see the outline of the house and barns.

Agatha dismounted, grabbed a pair of gloves from her saddlebag, and walked over to a small, fenced-off area. Inside were headstones, some older, some newer, and flowerbeds full of wildflowers that Agatha had planted herself. Tori followed along behind her.

“You can’t read it anymore, but this one belongs to Hiram, and this one is Agnes,” Agatha told her, pointing to two large but worn headstones. “These three are their children who died as babies or very young, Eliza, Martha, James… Then there’s Henry, he never married. Emma and her family are buried in the old cemetery closer to town, she married a preacher who helped found Westview. This is Nicholas, and his wife Hannah, and their five children. Their son James was your great-great grandfather. He married Rebekah, and they had three children. James the second is your great-grandfather, Grandpa Jim, the one who passed away a few months ago. Your great-grandmother’s name was Clara, she’s buried here. They had two sons, Elijah and Eric, and a daughter, Evanora. Evanora is my mother, your grandma.” Agatha sighed. “So that’s how we get all the way from Hiram Harkness to you, Tori Vidal.”

“I’m not a Harkness,” Tori noted.

“Not by name, maybe,” Agatha acknowledged. “But you’re just as much a Harkness as Nicky and Ollie. This place is yours as much as it is theirs, just like my name is. These are your ancestors, too. Their blood is your blood.”

Agatha got down on her hands and knees and began pulling weeds from the flowerbeds and the walkways between the graves.

“I thought you had ranchhands to do this?” Tori asked.

“The hands work on the ranch. I take care of my family myself,” Agatha told her. She tugged at a particularly stubborn weed and a giant dirt clod came out with it, sending dirt and dust flying all over Agatha’s shirt and into her face. Agatha sputtered and spit what got into her mouth.

Tori laughed, then looked around, a studious expression on her face. “I could help.”

Agatha raised a brow at her. “You sure?”

“They’re my ancestors, too,” Tori replied.

A smile tugged at Agatha’s lips. “There’s another pair of gloves in River’s saddlebag.”

Tori quickly retrieved the gloves and went to work, kneeling in the grass beside Agatha. It didn’t take them long to have the little graveyard looking neat and tidy again. When they were finished, Agatha got two bottles of water from her other saddle bag and handed one to Tori.

“Can I ask you a question?” Tori asked.

“Anything,” Agatha replied.

“What happened to grandma Evanora? Why don’t you talk to her? Why did the ranch go from Grandpa Jim to you and not to her?”

Agatha bit her lip, because technically her grandfather had left half of the ranch to Evanora, and now that was causing her a massive headache. But Agatha wasn’t about to put the weight of that knowledge onto Tori’s shoulders.

“The first thing you have to understand is that your Grandpa Jim wasn’t a good man,” Agatha said. “His own father, James, almost ran this place to the ground with bad financial decisions and just sheer bad luck. Grandpa Jim was determined to build it back up, and he didn’t care who he stepped on or stabbed in the back to prove it. Case and point, what happened between him and your other grandfather.”

Tori nodded in understanding.

“In addition to being an all-around asshole, he was also a giant misogynist,” Agatha continued. “So when he was raising his three kids, he focused all his time and attention on raising his sons to be cowboys and he didn’t really have anything to do with his only daughter.

“My mother’s reaction to this lack of male attention and affection was to leave town as soon as she could and move to the last place her father would ever care to look: Boston. And once she was there, she started an affair with a married man. A couple of years into the affair she got pregnant, and she thought that would make my father finally leave his wife and be with her. He laughed in her face and told her to get lost. The only thing he ever gave her after that was hush money to keep her from telling his wife about the affair or my existence.”

“That’s terrible,” Tori said, getting back onto Luna.

“Yes, my biological father is a terrible man. Hence why I have the last name Harkness,” Agatha explained. “My mother wasn’t particularly interested in being a mother, either, so as soon as I was old enough she forced my father to pay to send me to private boarding schools. And every summer she would send me here, to the ranch. Then, my junior year of high school, I got kicked out of that private boarding school for kissing one of my female classmates, so Mother sent me here permanently.”

“How did Grandpa Jim react to that?” Tori asked.

“Not well,” Agatha replied. “I mean, I already knew he was homophobic on top of everything else. Uncle Eric was gay, according to Lilia, and Grandpa Jim refused to acknowledge it and even kicked his boyfriend out of the funeral service after he died in a car accident. But by the time I moved here, Uncle Eric was gone, Uncle Elijah was gone, and my mother had zero interest in coming back. If my grandfather wanted the ranch to stay in the family, the only descendent he had to pass it onto was his lesbian granddaughter.”

“Oh, wow,” Tori said, letting out a humorless chuckle.

“Yes, the irony is kind of beautiful, isn’t it?” Agatha said with a laugh. “I was never under the illusion that Grandpa had high expectations for me to take over this place. In fact, I’m pretty sure he lived to be ninety-four just because he didn’t want to pass this place onto me, he was that convinced that I was going to run it into the ground. But that just made me work harder. It’s made me even more determined to keep this place going, and more than that, have it grow and become even bigger and better than he did.”

“Just out of spite?” Tori asked.

“Just out of spite,” Agatha confirmed. Then she shook her head. “Well, no. I shouldn’t say that. It’s more than spite that keeps me going.”

“Then what is it?” Tori asked.

Agatha looked at the trees and field around them and spread her arms. “You see all this? One hundred and forty years ago, Hiram and Agnes Harkness looked out over these fields and said, This is it, this is our home. And then they build that cabin with their own two hands. Then Nicholas Harkness decided to start raising cattle. His son almost lost it, but Grandpa James built it back. It’s…” Agatha paused and looked at the sky. “This ranch, this land, is something that multiple generations of our family poured their blood, sweat, and tears into. They built something. And I want to be part of that. I want to keep building and expanding and making this place something beautiful and worthwhile for you and for your brother and sister. Does that make sense?”

Tori studied her, then nodded. “Yeah. That’s… That’s kind of beautiful.”

Agatha beamed at her. “I’m glad you think so.”

When they got to the barn, Nicky was riding Scratchy in the arena, and Rio was sitting on the fence watching her.

“Hey kiddo!” Rio greeted. She looked from Tori to Agatha curiously. “What have you two been up to?”

“I was just showing her around the place,” Agatha replied.

“Mama showed me the old homestead, and the family graveyard,” Tori explained. “It was really cool.”

“Cool, huh?” Rio asked. Tori nodded, a wide smile on her face.

Agatha looked at her daughters and the barn behind them, the house on the hill, and the fields that stretched for miles in every direction. Maybe, just maybe, this ranch had a future after all.

Chapter End Notes

Listen, if I got the number of “greats” wrong at some point just go with it, even when editing it broke my brain trying to count.

Chapter 17: Rio

Chapter Summary

Rio checks out a house and the family celebrates Tori’s birthday

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“This is… interesting.”

Rio checked the address on the rental ad against the numbers on the house in front of her again. “Yeah, it’s… something.”

The house looked like someone had sandwiched together two different houses. The main part of the house was two stories, made of dark brick, with wooden shutters. At some point, someone had built an addition on the right side of the house that was only one story and covered in ugly tan vinyl. A small lean-to barn sat out back along with a small pasture. The property had once belonged to the parents of one of Rio’s veterinary clients, but they had passed away a year ago and now the man was looking to rent or sell.

“Let’s go look inside,” Rio said, leading the way to the door. The owner had left her instructions to find the key in the false bottom of a flowerpot on the front steps, and once she found it she opened the door.

“Hello shag carpet,” Alice said, stepping through the door. Her nose wrinkled as soon as she was inside. “It smells like old people.”

Rio sniffed and wrinkled her nose as well. “I think they had cats.”

“Ew,” Alice said.

“Frank said he’d pay for removal of the carpet and installation of new flooring if I’d cover materials,” Rio told her. “If I agree to a rent-to-own arrangement.”

“Uh-huh,” Alice said, looking up at a stain on the popcorn ceiling. “What about a new roof and plumbing repairs?”

Rio looked up at the stain. “We didn’t discuss that.”

“You might want to,” Alice told her. “Let’s check out the kitchen.”

The kitchen was dated but functional. It was bigger than Mateo’s trailer, but that wasn’t saying much. It was in the addition, along with a sunroom that could double as a breakfast nook. There was also a small bedroom downstairs that could work for one of the girls, or as an office, and a bathroom with olive green tile that hadn’t been updated since the seventies.

“Let’s go upstairs,” Rio said, not sold on the house at all.

“Did you tell the girls you were coming to look at a house?”

“No,” Rio replied. “I wasn’t sure how they’d react.”

“Right…” Alice said, rolling her eyes. She paused at the top of the stairs. “Oh, look, more shag carpet.”

“What do you mean right?” Rio asked.

“I mean you know exactly how they’d react,” Alice replied. “Badly.”

Rio frowned as they looked around upstairs. There was a decent-sized landing and two bedrooms, each with its own attached bathroom.

“It’s not so bad,” Rio said, looking around at one of the bathrooms. This one had mauve tile and decor. “It needs some updating, but I could make it work. It has room for me and the girls, plus there’s a place for the horses.”

“Rio,” Alice said, her tone exasperated, “this place sucks.”

Rio looked around at the ancient tile and sighed. “It’s not—”

“Rio—”

“Okay, yeah, it sucks,” Rio agreed. “But it’s the only decent-sized place I’ve been able to find in my budget. Most of the houses in town have been bought up by flippers and now they’re too expensive. And any rentals are just one bedrooms or studio apartments. My only other option is to move closer to Bozeman, but that would be a hell of a commute, plus it would uproot the girls.” Rio sighed. “I’m out of options.”

“Is Agatha kicking you out?”

“No.” Rio made her way back downstairs as she spoke. “She says I can stay with her for as long as I need to.”

“So what’s the problem?”

They went outside and Rio locked the door behind them. But instead of heading back to the truck, she sat on the edge of the porch, looking out over the front yard of the house.

“I can’t stay there, Alice,” she said. “It’s too much.”

“What do you mean?” Alice asked, sitting beside her.

“Agatha said something, when Tori and I first went to stay with her,” Rio said. “She said that the reason she didn’t tell me that she was pregnant was because she knew I would give everything up to come back and be with her. And that if I did that, eventually the regret and resentment would suffocate me.”

Alice nodded. “Is that what’s happening now? Is she suffocating you?”

Rio didn’t answer immediately, trying to find the words that would truly describe what she was feeling. Finally she shook her head.

“No, I’m not suffocating. Not exactly.”

“Then what is it?” Alice asked. “You can tell me, you know.”

Rio took a long, shuddering breath. “A long time ago, I loved Agatha. I still loved her when I left Westview. But I still left. Because after dreaming of leaving for so long, I couldn’t just stay here. I had made this plan and I was obligated to follow it, to see it through.”

“And Agatha wasn’t part of that plan,” Alice finished for her.

Rio nodded. “By the time we broke up, I was so damn confused that I didn’t even want to leave. Not really. And I didn’t want to hurt her. But I did. And I carried it around all these years like… like a scar.”

“A scar?”

“She is my scar,” Rio said, reaching up and wiping her eyes. “Living with her, it’s like that wound has been torn wide open all over again. Like my insides are just exposed and raw. And even though she’s not poking at it, everything she does feels like a knife stabbing me again and again.”

Alice was quiet for a long time. Rio dried her tears and leaned forward onto her knees, trying to gather her composure again.

“You said that you loved Agatha when you left Westview,” Alice said finally. “Did you ever really stop loving her?”

“I tried to,” Rio replied. “When I thought that she had rejected me and Tori. I thought I stopped. But then I found out the truth and now…”

“You’re in love with her?”

“I don’t know,” Rio said. “We’re different people now. I don’t know if I’m in love with her or in love with a ghost of her.”

“What’s stopping you from finding out?”

“What do you mean?”

“I mean what’s stopping you from telling her how you feel and seeing what happens?” Alice asked. “C’mon, Rio, you have to admit that you’ve at least thought about it.”

“Sure I’ve thought about it,” Rio replied. “But then I remember that she lied and kept my daughter from me for seventeen years.”

“Technically she didn’t lie, she just didn’t tell you,” Alice pointed out.

“A lie by omission is still a lie, Alice. It still fucking hurts,” Rio growled out. “Even if I could find it in myself to forgive her— which I haven’t, I might add— what if she doesn’t feel the same way? What if we try to work things out and it falls apart again. Agatha has a tendency to run away just for the thrill of being chased, and frankly I’m tired of it. That’s why I broke up with her, in the end. I was sick and tired of being the one to constantly chase her just so she felt validated in the relationship. And then, when the tables were turned, she didn’t—”

Rio cut herself off, biting the inside of her jaw so hard that she tasted blood. She swallowed hard, fighting down the tears that threatened to fall once again.

“I chased her for so many years, and in the end she couldn’t be bothered to return the favor,” Rio spat. “No more, Alice. If she wants a relationship, she has to be the one to take the first step. She has to be the one who does the chasing. I’m through.”

The end of April bled into May. May brought warmer temperatures and flowering fields and calving season and Tori’s seventeenth birthday. It fell on a school night, so they didn’t plan much of a celebration. Instead, Rio and Tori spent two hours in the waiting room of the DMV, waiting for Tori’s chance to take her driver’s test. The wait was unbearable, and Rio could practically feel the anxiety coming off of Tori in waves. She was literally trembling by the time they called her back. Rio wasn’t surprised when Tori returned to the office in tears, and the poor DMV employee shook his head sadly at Rio as he passed.

By the time they got back to the ranch, Tori’s tears had dried up. Instead she was sullen, not speaking to Rio when she tried to ask her what had gone wrong in the test. When they got to the ranch, instead of heading to the dining room where everyone else was waiting, Tori turned and ran upstairs. Rio watched her go and sighed before heading down the hall to deliver the news.

“Happy Bir— Where’s Tori?” Ollie asked. He was wearing a pointed party hat, and there were sparkly purple streamers pinned to the walls around the table.

“She didn’t pass the driving test,” Rio told them. “She’s a little upset, so she went to her room.”

“But Remy made nachos. Those are her favorite,” Ollie said. “And we have cake.”

“I don’t think she’s in the mood right now, Ollie,” Rio said.

“I’ll go check on her,” Nicky volunteered, pushing her chair back and taking off her party hat before going upstairs.

“What happened?” Agatha asked.

“She wouldn’t tell me,” Rio replied. “But she was really nervous when they called her back. She’s a decent driver, but she gets anxious about things like this.”

Agatha raised a brow. “I wonder who she gets that from?”

Rio sat in her usual seat. Ollie looked back and forth between her and Agatha and then at the plates of food in front of them.

“Can we eat now?”

“No, hon, we need to wait for your sisters,” Agatha replied.

“But… I’m hungry,” he said pitifully.

“Go ahead, Ollie,” Rio told him. “Who knows how long they’ll be.”

“Really?” Ollie asked, perking up.

“Really,” Rio assured him.

After ten minutes or so, Nicky and Tori returned to the dining room. Tori’s eyes were still red-rimmed, and her hair was a mess, but she was clearly trying to pull herself together for their celebration.

“There’s the birthday girl,” Agatha said with a smile. She stood and picked up the sparkly plastic crown from Tori’s spot at the table and placed it on Tori’s head. “Happy Birthday, sweetheart.”

“Thanks, Mama,” Tori said, a genuine smile pulling at her lips.

They ate nachos and exchanged gifts. Nicky gave Tori a new sketchbook and a set of colored pencils. Ollie gave her a pencil pouch made from purple fabric with a kitten and rainbow print. Finally it was Rio and Agatha’s turn, and for once they had worked together on something.

“Well, there’s a small problem with our gift,” Rio said, reaching into her pocket. “You can’t use it quite yet.”

She pulled out a set of keys with a purple rabbit’s foot keychain. Tori’s jaw instantly dropped.

“You got me a car?” she asked.

“We got you a truck,” Agatha corrected. “You need something that can haul a horse trailer, afterall.”

“Oh my god,” Tori said.

“It’s outside, if you want to go see it,” Rio told her.

They all headed outside. Lilia had driven the truck up from the barn once Rio and Tori got home, and she posed beside it like Vanna White when they all came out of the house. It was secondhand, like Nicky’s had been, but in good shape. Where Nicky’s truck was olive green, Tori’s was black.

“This is so cool,” Tori said, but Rio could tell she was holding back her excitement. “But what if I can’t pass my driving test?”

“I’ll practice with you,” Rio assured her.

“But you’ve been so busy with work,” Tori groused. “We’ll never have time.”

“I can work with you,” Agatha interjected. “How soon can you take the test again?”

“Two weeks,” Tori replied.

“We’ll practice every afternoon,” Agatha promised.

“And if Agatha’s busy, I can teach you,” Lilia offered. “Afterall, I was the one who taught your Mama.”

“Really?” Tori asked, looking between the two women excitedly.

“Really,” Lilia nodded.

It was starting to get dark and they were about to go inside for cake when they spotted headlights coming up the drive. Rio squinted in the low light as the truck got closer, and then she realized who it was.

“Fuck,” she muttered. “You guys should go inside.”

Tori stepped beside her. “Is that Tito?”

“Looks like it,” Rio grumbled.

“Ollie, why don’t you take Lilia inside for some nachos?” Agatha said.

“Yeah, buddy, let’s go,” Lilia agreed, taking the little boy into the house.

“You girls should go inside, too,” Rio said.

“But it’s Tito,” Tori said.

Before Rio could argue further, the truck pulled up in front of the house and parked. Her father didn’t turn off the ignition before he stepped out, which meant he didn’t plan to stay long.

“You’re not supposed to be driving, Papi,” Rio said.

“I didn’t go far,” he scoffed. “I just wanted to see my granddaughter on her birthday.”

Rio stared at him angrily, but when she looked at Tori she could see the torn emotions in her eyes. She sighed and nudged her daughter.

“Give your grandpa a hug,” she said.

Tori stepped forward and hugged Mateo tightly. “Hi, Tito.”

“Happy birthday, nieta,” Mateo said. When he let her go, he reached into his back pocket and pulled out an envelope. “I brought you a present. It’s not much, but—”

“You didn’t have to do that,” Tori said, but Mateo just waved her off. Tori opened the envelope; inside was a storebought birthday card, and inside that was a twenty-dollar bill. “Gracias, Tito.”

“De nada, nieta,” Mateo replied. He looked around at the other angry faces looking at him. “I supposed I better get back home. Te amo, nieta. Te amo, mija.”

He started to turn toward the truck when a shout from the porch startled all of them.

“What about me, motherfucker?” Nicky shouted, stomping down the steps.

Mateo turned around, his face white with shock. Nicky stopped a few feet away from him, looking at him with angry, tear-filled eyes.

“I’m your granddaughter, too,” she said. “Were you even going to say hello?”

“Mija, are you really going to let her speak to me that way?” Mateo asked.

“Are you going to answer her?” Rio asked in return.

Mateo scoffed and muttered something about Harknesses under his breath before turning back toward his truck.

“Yeah, that figures,” Nicky scoffed. “Just pretend I don’t fucking exist, just like you have for the last seventeen years.”

“Nicky, sweetheart—” Agatha began.

“Tito, wait!” Tori called as Mateo closed his truck door. She hurried toward the truck, and Mateo rolled the window down. Tori took the card he had given her, money and all, and held it out to him. “Take it.”

Mateo scowled. “It’s a gift, nieta.”

“I don’t want it,” Tori said. “If you can’t even acknowledge my sister, I don’t want anything else from you ever again.”

She dropped the card into his lap and stepped back from the truck. Mateo looked at her and then at Rio, his frown deepening, before he changed the gears in his truck and pulled away.

Rio moved to her daughter’s side. Tori’s eyes were damp, but she held her chin up proudly. Rio wrapped her arms around her and kissed her cheek.

“I’m proud of you, mija.”

“He doesn’t get to just ignore her,” Tori declared. “Not anymore.”

When they turned back toward the house, Nicky immediately grabbed Tori in a tight hug. They didn’t speak, just held each other for a minute.

Finally, Agatha cleared her throat. “I think there might be a lemon and blueberry birthday cake waiting inside.”

Tori’s head shot up. “Lemon blueberry? Really?”

“A little birdie told me we have the same favorite flavor,” Agatha told her, nudging Nicky’s shoulder as she did so.

The rest of the evening was happier, but Rio could still see the shadow of her father’s visit hanging over the girls, especially Nicky. Once they had gone upstairs to get ready for bed, she went to her room and dug around her belongings. She finally found the small leather case she was looking for and took it down the hall to the girls’ room.

“Knock knock,” she said, pushing the door open slowly. The girls were in their pajamas already, both sitting on the bottom bunk bed. They scooted over so that Rio could sit on the end of the bed.

“What’s up, Mami?” Tori asked.

“Well, I know it’s your birthday today,” Rio said. “But since I missed Nicky’s birthday a few months ago, I thought you might not mind if I gave her a gift today.”

Tori nodded as Nicky’s eyes widened. Rio handed her the leather case, and she took it reverently.

“I didn’t have a chance to wrap it,” Rio told her, chagrined.

“What is it?” Nicky asked.

“Open it and see,” Rio coaxed.

Nicky unzipped the pouch and gasped when she saw the green stethoscope inside.

“Oh my god,” Nicky said excitedly. “Is this real?”

“It’s the real deal,” Rio told her. “It was my first stethoscope. I got it my first year at UC Davis.”

“This is so cool,” Nicky exclaimed. She threw herself at Rio, almost tackling her to the bed. “Thank you, Mami!”

Rio chuckled and wrapped her arms around her daughter. “You’re welcome, mija.”

Nicky beamed at her, then looked toward the door. “Look, Mama! Look what Mami gave me!”

Rio thought that Agatha was still putting Ollie to bed, but instead she was leaning against the doorframe, watching the exchange with a fond expression. “I see, babygirl.”

“I wanna try it out,” Nicky said, putting the earpieces in her ears. “Tori, lemme listen to you.”

Rio showed her how to find a heartbeat. Nicky had to experiment on all of them, and she even took Draco out of his enclosure to try it out on him. The bearded dragon was less than enthused. They had to stop her from taking the stethoscope down to the barn in the middle of the night. She finally tucked the stethoscope back into its case and placed it in her nightstand before going to bed.

“Goodnight, girls,” Rio said, closing the door as she and Agatha stepped out of the bedroom.

“Goodnight, moms!” they both called in unison.

Rio chuckled as the door latched behind her. Agatha leaned against the wall across from the door, a bittersweet expression on her face.

“What’s wrong?” Rio asked.

“Nothing,” Agatha said quickly.

Rio studied her for a moment, then nodded. “Well… Goodnight.”

She was almost to the guestroom door when Agatha spoke again. “Rio?”

Rio turned back to her. “Yeah?”

“I was wrong,” Agatha whispered.

“About what?”

Agatha swallowed hard. “You know what.”

She crossed her arms and turned toward her own room. “Goodnight, Rio.”

“Goodnight, Agatha,” Rio replied, standing frozen in the doorway as the lights went out.

Chapter End Notes

You’re allowed to hate Mateo. It’s ok.

Chapter 18: Nicky

Chapter Summary

Nicky learns that being a vet isn’t always cute and fun

Chapter Notes

CW: animal euthanasia

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Nicky’s alarm hadn’t gone off yet when Rio shook her awake. Nicky stared up at her blearily as Rio shushed her and beckoned her to follow. Nicky put on a hoodie and tucked her Mickey Mouse pajama pants into her boots before following Rio outside and down to the cattle barn.

“It’s too early,” Nicky complained as they trudged down the gravel drive.

“Get used to it, mija. Vets keep all hours, especially during calving season,” Rio told her. “And believe me, you’ll want to see this.”

Nicky yawned. “I’ve seen calves before.”

Rio just smirked and led her through the barn. Unlike the horse barn that had individual stalls, the cattle barn was separated by metal railing into four pens of various sizes, with a chute at one end. The herds spent most of the year roaming freely on the property, but once calving season began the ranchhands would round the expectant mothers up and bring them to the pasture closest to the barn for monitoring.

“Jimmy saw this girl struggling, so they brought her in and called me down to help,” Rio explained as they came to the last pen. “And it’s a good thing he did, because she never would’ve passed her calf otherwise.”

Nicky stepped up beside her and peered into the stall. At first all she could see was the cow, a solid black cow except for her white face. Then Nicky saw the calf at her side. At first glance it looked to be pretty big, definitely a healthy weight. But as Nicky’s eyes adjusted to the light, she could see something strange coming out of the calf’s back close to its shoulders: an extra leg, smaller than it should be, hanging uselessly beside the normal front leg. The calf was trying to nurse, but after a minute it stopped, bleating pitifully as it turned. That was when Nicky saw its head. It was a baldy, like its mother, which made the deformities even more obvious. It had two snouts, each pointing in a different direction, both with cleft palates, four nostrils, three eyes, and two ears.

“It has two heads,” Nicky said, stating the obvious. “And an extra leg.”

“Yep,” Rio nodded.

“Will it survive?” Nicky asked, finally looking away from the calf to look at her mother. She knew the answer before Rio replied, just from the expression on her face.

“We left it for the night to see if it would nurse, but because of its cleft palate it can’t get a good latch,” Rio explained. “The best thing for it, unfortunately, is to humanely euthanize it.”

“You’re just giving up on it?” Nicky asked, her eyes filling with tears. “Why can’t you bottle feed it or tube feed it? Surely you can do something.”

“Nicky, sweetheart, it’ll never live a normal life,” Rio told her. “Sure, we could keep it alive by tube feeding, but that brings its own risk of issues, plus it’s stressful. And then when he’s older, we’d still have to do surgery to repair his cleft palates, which might not even be possible. And, ultimately, this is a beef cow. We’d be doing all that just so it could grow for a few years and then be slaughtered for meat. It doesn’t make any sense.”

“But… he’s just a baby,” Nicky argued.

“I know,” Rio sighed. “And it’s okay to be sad. It’s okay to not like it. But we also have to be realistic. This is part of our job as vets, and it’s part of the job of any rancher, any pet owner really. Sometimes you have to weigh the pros and cons and do what’s best for an animal. And sometimes what’s best for them is to let them go.”

Nicky wiped angrily at her eyes. Suddenly a warm weight settled on her shoulders, and she realized Rio had put her arm around her shoulders. Nicky immediately turned and buried her face in her mother’s shirt, her emotions getting the best of her.

“Think of it this way,” Rio said, “he’s never known pain. He’s never known discomfort. All he’s ever had to know is a warm stall and his mama’s love. His life might be short, but we can make it good.”

Nicky sniffed her tears away. “Can we take him outside before you do it? He should feel the sunshine before he goes.”

Rio’s face softened. “Yeah, mija, we can do that.”

With the help of a couple ranchhands they moved the calf into a small pen outside. The calf toddled around for a moment before finally lying down in the grass. His black fur glistened in the sunshine, and its pink noses twitched as it sniffed the breeze.

Agatha joined them shortly, and then Rio went to her truck to prepare the medication. She looked at her daughter as if taking a measure of her. “You sure you wanna be here for this?”

“Yes,” Nicky replied. “I want to be here.”

Agatha nodded solemnly. “One of the other cows had twins last week and she keeps kicking the smaller baby off when it tries to feed. We’re gonna see if this mama will adopt that one once her baby passes on.”

Nicky nodded. “That’s good.”

Rio returned with the syringe and her stethoscope a few minutes later. Agatha watched from the edge of the pen while Rio and Nicky attended to the calf.

“Nicky, can you hold his head?” Rio asked. Nicky sat in the grass and let the calf rest its head in her lap. She held it still as Rio found the right spot and injected the medication. “Good, that’s good. Easy, little guy. It’s okay.”

A few moments later, it was done. Nicky felt the life fade from the little calf as it went limp in her lap. She felt tears stinging her eyes again, and she ducked her head to press a kiss to the side of the calf’s face.

“There we go, it’s all over,” Rio sighed, taking her stethoscope out of her ears. “You did good, sweetheart. Now I want you to go in the house and get ready for school. I called the clinic and told them we would be late, but you still need to get dressed.”

“But I want to help with the other calf,” Nicky said automatically, blinking away the tears in her eyes.

“Nicky,” Rio said, her voice serious, “in a few minutes, we’re going to take the skin off of this calf and put it onto an orphan calf so that his mama will adopt it. It’s the best possible outcome for this, but it’s not pretty. You’ve done really well, but I don’t want you to see that. Not yet. Trust me, okay?”

Nicky nodded and wiped her eyes. “I’m sorry that I’m crying. Grandpa Jim always said there’s no crying in ranching.”

“Grandpa Jim was a heartless bastard,” Agatha spat.

“Don’t ever be ashamed that you care,” Rio told her. “That’s what makes you a good person, and it’s what’s going to make you a great vet someday. But for now, just go inside, okay?”

Nicky gave the dead calf one more squeeze before getting up and hurrying inside. Tori and Ollie were already dressed and at the breakfast table, but Nicky just hurried past them. By the time she came back downstairs, Agatha had already taken them to school. Nicky grabbed a granola bar from the kitchen for breakfast and headed outside. She was almost to her truck when she heard her name being shouted. She turned to see Rio running toward her from the barn, holding onto her hat with one hand.

“Mami?” she said, confused.

“Come with me,” Rio said, reaching for her hand. “I already called the clinic and told them you won’t be there today.”

Rio led her back down to the cattle barn, to the stall where the two-headed calf’s mother was. The cow was still there, but there was a different calf with her. This one only had one head, and no deformities, but its little face was almost perfectly split in half, one side black and one side white. There was something tied to its torso, and after a moment Nicky realized it was the skin from the calf that had died. At first it seemed gross, but then she saw the cow turn around and lick the calf, and she understood.

“She thinks it’s her baby?” Nicky asked.

“It is her baby now,” Rio said. “Watch.”

The calf let out a low bellow, then went to the cow’s udder. He headbutted her roughly before lowering his head and starting to nurse. In spite of herself, Nicky found her lips tugging up in a smile.

“See?” Rio said. “Out of death comes life.”

“Thank you,” Nicky said. “I did need to see that.”

“It’s all part of being a vet. You get used to it, but it never stops hurting when you lose one, especially a baby. It’s nice when something positive can come out of it,” Rio told her. “It’s part of being a rancher, too. You have to understand the balance of life and death, especially when you take over this place.”

Nicky bit her tongue. “Yeah… Sure.”

Rio’s brow crinkled in confusion. “Mija?”

“Can I tell you something?” Nicky asked, her words coming out faster than she meant.

“Of course,” Rio assured her.

“You have to promise not to tell Mama,” Nicky added, a rapid whisper.

“Scouts’ honor,” Rio replied, giving her a two-finger salute.

Nicky blew out a long breath and looked back at the cow and calf. “It’s not a big deal. It’s just… I don’t know if I want to take over running this place. I know that’s what Mama wants me to do, eventually, but… I don’t know what I want. I just know that I want to see more of the world than Westview before I decide.”

Rio stared at her for a long moment, then she dropped her head so that Nicky couldn’t see her face. Her shoulders started shaking, and for a second Nicky thought she might be crying, but then Nicky realized that she was laughing.

“Ugh— I shouldn’t have said anything,” Nicky huffed, pushing herself away from the fencing and turning to go back up the hill to her truck.

“Nicky, wait,” Rio said, her voice still shaky with laughter. “I’m sorry. I just… It’s funny.”

“No it’s not,” Nicky huffed. Rio caught her by the shoulder and turned her back around to face her.

“What you told me isn’t funny,” Rio said seriously. “What’s funny is how alike you and I are.” Rio stood back, staring at her with a smirk. “God, you might look like Agatha and she might’ve raised you, but you’re definitely my kid, mija.”

Nicky felt her cheeks flush at Rio’s words. Rio put an arm around her shoulders, and Nicky went into her embrace willingly.

“Do you think Mama would be mad if I told her?” Nicky asked.

“No,” Rio said with certainty. “A little disappointed, maybe. But she wouldn’t be mad. Your mama loves you kids more than anything in the world, including this ranch. She’d burn the whole thing to the ground if it meant you were happy.”

“How do you know?” Nicky asked.

Rio looked at her wistfully and sighed. “When I was your age, I dreamed about traveling around the world.”

“Really?” Nicky asked.

“Yep,” Rio replied.

“Did Mama know?”

Rio bit her lip. “Yeah, she knew. Your mama was the only person who supported my dreams. My parents didn’t understand. Most of the people in town didn’t understand. But your mama always thought I could do anything I set my mind to. She encouraged me to apply for UC Davis, and to go chase all my crazy dreams. She wanted me to be happy, even if it meant she and I didn’t end up together.”

“Why didn’t Mama just go with you?” Nicky asked. “Why did she want this stupid ranch so bad?”

“This ranch isn’t stupid,” Rio told her. “This ranch is your family’s legacy.”

“Yeah, but our family sucks,” Nicky argued. “Grandpa Jim was a dick. Grandma Evanora is a bitch. Neither of them treated Mama like they should have. If I was her, I would’ve run away with you.”

Rio sighed. “Your mama is a stubborn woman. It’s her best and worst feature. At some point, she decided that she was going to prove everyone wrong. She was going to take over this ranch, and not only was she going to keep it going, she was going to make it thrive, no matter what. And, from what I’ve seen, she’s succeeded.”

“So stupid,” Nicky muttered. “You two should’ve just stayed together.”

“Which of us should’ve given up our dreams, mija?” Rio asked. “I couldn’t ask your mom to give up this ranch, and she wouldn’t ask me to give up my aspirations, either. We loved each other too much for that.”

“But neither of you loved the other one enough to give it up without being asked,” Nicky pointed out.

Rio’s face fell, and she looked pained, like Nicky’s words caused her physical pain. “No… I guess we didn’t.”

“If Mama had told you about me, would you have stayed?” Nicky asked, the question she had held in for weeks escaping before she could rein it back in.

Rio reached out and cupped Nicky’s jaw in her hand, tears welling up in her dark eyes.

“Wild horses couldn’t have dragged me away, mija,” she said, her voice breaking as the tears fell down her cheeks.

Nicky couldn’t help herself. She wrapped her arms around Rio’s waist and hugged her tightly. Her mother held her back just as tight, resting her chin atop her head.

“I’m glad you came back to Westview. Even if it isn’t what you wanted,” Nicky mumbled into Rio’s shoulder.

“I’m glad I came back, too,” Rio agreed.

Chapter End Notes

Also if you caught the reference to another spectacular Agathario fic, yay!

Chapter 19: Tori

Chapter Summary

Driving lessons with Mama

The lunchroom was full to bursting when Tori sat down at the table with her friends. Teddy and Cassie were studying for a history final, Nicky and Tommy were finishing a biology worksheet, and Yelena and Kate were practically on top of one another discussing prom plans. The dance was the following weekend, but Tori and Nicky weren’t going, because they were competing in a rodeo out of town.

Billy sat down beside her with a groan. “I swear, Ms. Schaeffer is going insane with the prom decorations.”

“I heard she really went all out this year,” Tommy commented. “What’s the theme again?”

“Out of this World,” Tori replied. Their English class had spent the last period putting together decorations while some students caught up on missing work. “There’s a lot of stars and planets involved.”

“You can still buy a ticket, you know,” Billy told his brother.

“Yeah, just because you’re not going with Morgan doesn’t mean you shouldn’t go at all,” Cassie pointed out.

“Nah, I’m good,” Tommy said, his cheeks flushing. “What kind of dork goes to prom by themselves, anyway?”

It might’ve been just a snide comment, but Tori saw how Tommy’s eyes cut towards Nicky. She elbowed Billy in the ribs and he grunted before looking up at his brother, his eyes widening.

“You could ask someone to go with you,” Tori said, trying to see how far she could push the boy. “Even if it’s just as a friend. Or, you know… more than a friend.”

Tommy’s cheeks turned even more pink and he shook his head so that his shaggy hair fell into his face to cover it. “I mean, I could, but it just doesn’t feel right, you know?”

“Oh?” Tori asked, her voice rising in pitch. “How so?”

Nicky looked up at her with narrowed eyes. “You’re being weird.”

“I’m not being weird,” Tori defended. “I’m just encouraging our friend to go have a good time. Unless there’s a reason he doesn’t want to go out with someone else—”

“Hey, I’ve been meaning to ask, how’s Project Agathario going?” Tommy asked, changing the subject.

Nicky and Tori groaned simultaneously.

“We are not calling them that,” Tori huffed.

“What? It’s their ship name!” Tommy exclaimed. “Like Brangelina and Kimye and Destiel.”

“Our mothers are not the Titanic,” Nicky told him.

“Also, two of those couples are divorced and the other is a fictional gay ship that never became canon,” Tori pointed out.

“They’re canon in the Latin America dub,” Tommy argued.

“Hey, focus,” Yelena interrupted, snapping her fingers. “I actually wanted to hear the update on the toxic yuri mothers.”

“They’re not toxic,” Nicky defended, then added under her breath, “Not anymore, anyway.”

“Yeah, they’re actually getting along now,” Tori told them. “Which… might be worse than the fighting, actually.”

“How so?” Cassie asked.

“Well, when they were fighting, there was this tension beneath the surface,” Tori explained.

Kate’s eyebrows shot up. “Sexual tension?”

“Ew, no,” Tori gagged.

“Well…” Nicky said, her voice rising in pitch before trailing off.

Tori glared at her. “Okay, maybe. But at the very least, it was obvious that they still cared for each other. Like, you could tell that they still had feelings for each other, even if those feelings were a little violent.”

“You’re not beating the toxic yuri accusations,” Yelena argued. Billy nodded in agreement.

“Well, they’re not toxic anymore,” Tori said. “They’re not really anything anymore. They don’t argue. They do talk, but it always seems to be about us. They’re civil but somehow that’s even worse than them fighting because it’s like they don’t even care. They’re just… existing in the same space.”

“Oh, that’s bad,” Teddy said. “That’s basically how my parents acted before they got divorced.”

“Exactly,” Tori nodded. “And our moms aren’t even together, so I feel like that’s an even worse sign.”

“What are you gonna do?” Kate asked.

“What can we do?” Tori asked rhetorically.

“You need to force them to confront their feelings for each other,” Cassie said. “That’s what happens in all the romance novels.”

“You mean that’s what happens in all the fanfics you read?” Kate teased.

“Hey, that is quality literature!” Cassie defended.

“No, no, she has a point,” Yelena argued. “Maybe you do need to force them together.”

“What are we supposed to do, lock them in a room together and hope they don’t kill each other?” Nicky asked.

“Perhaps not so dramatically,” Yelena conceded.

“What happens in your fanfictions?” Billy asked, looking at Cassie.

“Well, I was reading a Heated Rivalry fanfic the other day—” Cassie began.

“Ew, men,” Kate gagged.

“Gay men,” Teddy pointed out.

“As I was saying,” Cassie continued, giving them a pointed look, “in the fic I was reading, Shane and Ilya are denying their feelings hard and then they accidentally book a hotel room that only has one bed—”

“Oh my god, there was only one bed!” Billy exclaimed dramatically. They all burst into laughter, and by the time they caught their breath, Tori’s stomach was aching.

“Fuck, I love you guys,” Nicky laughed, wiping a tear from the corner of her eye.

“I don’t know if that helped, but I tried,” Cassie shrugged.

Suddenly Tori had an idea. “Hey! We do have that rodeo trip coming up.”

“Yeah, but Mama already booked the rooms,” Nicky pointed out.

“I know,” Tori smirked. “But wouldn’t it be a shame if someone changed the reservation to a room with a single bed?”

Nicky stared at her for a moment before her face melted into a nearly-identical grin. “Oh, that’s genius.”

“Damn, you two really are sisters,” Billy commented, staring at them with wide eyes.

“That’s fucking terrifying,” Yelena added.

“Diabolical,” Kate agreed.

Tori’s grin widened. “Let’s do it.”

After dismissal, Tori made her way to the elementary side of the school. Nicky had left early for an orthodontist appointment, so she was going to walk Ollie to the carline to meet Agatha. She weaved through the halls, nodding politely to the teachers leading the younger kids in single-file lines, until she came to the EC room.

“Ms. Grey? I’m here to pick up Ollie,” she called, knocking on the door.

“Tori!” Ollie shouted, running across the classroom to her. He stopped a foot away and greeted her with a fist-bump. “We’re going on a field trip to the zoo!”

The red-haired woman smiled as she brought Ollie’s backpack over. “You must be this new sister Ollie’s been telling us about.”

Tori blushed. “Yeah, that would be me.”

“Well, he absolutely adores you,” Ms. Grey told her. “Could you tell your mom that he has a permission slip in his folder?”

“Yes, ma’am, I will,” Tori replied. “You ready to go, Ollie?”

“Yep!” Ollie replied, grabbing her hand as they walked out of the classroom. “I wonder if they’ll have chickens at the zoo?”

“They might,” Tori said. “You know, Mami-Rio used to work at a zoo.”

“Really?” Ollie asked, his face lighting up.

“Yep,” Tori nodded. “Sometimes I would get to go to work with her. It was really cool.”

“Why’d she quit?” Ollie asked.

“She quit so we could move here,” Tori told him. “We had to help take care of Tito, my grandpa.”

“The mean one?” Ollie asked.

Tori frowned. “Yeah, unfortunately.”

“But she’s not taking care of him now,” Ollie pointed out. “So why doesn’t she go back and work at the zoo?”

“Because the zoo’s really far away.”

“Ms. Grey says we’ll be on a bus for almost two hours,” Ollie whined. “That’s a long time.”

“Mami-Rio didn’t work at the zoo you’re going to visit, buddy. The one she worked at was in California.”

Ollie’s brow crinkled in confusion. “Is that like… three hours away?”

“I think it’s like… twenty-one hours,” Tori told him.

“Nobody drives for twenty-one hours. That’s impossible,” Ollie declared with certainty.

“Hi, Mama!” Ollie greeted. “We’re going to the zoo!”

“Oh, are we?” Agatha replied.

“Ms. Grey said there’s a permission form in his backpack,” Tori told her.

“Thank you, sweetheart.” Agatha tossed her the keys and Tori caught them on reflex. “You ready for driving practice?”

Tori’s eyes widened. “With you? And with Ollie?”

“Yes,” Agatha nodded.

Tori gulped. “Are you sure?”

“I moved his booster seat into your truck. He’ll be fine,” Agatha assured her. “Let’s go! Vamanos!”

“Okay, kid, let’s see what you’ve got.”

“Ouch!” Ollie exclaimed when his head hit the seat behind him as Tori hit the brakes again, afraid she was getting too close to the car and would hit it.

“Sorry, bud,” Tori apologized. She started to go forward but—

“Stop!” Agatha shouted. Tori hit the brakes again. “You have to change gears, sweetheart.”

“Sorry, sorry!” Tori put the truck in drive and pulled forward, turning her wheel sharply. She sat up in her seat, arching her neck as she pulled out of the parking lot and onto the main road. She was okay for a bit, until they got into town.

“Turn right at the next light,” Agatha instructed.

Tori bit her lip and put on her turn signal. She eased into the turning lane, but there were cars parallel parked on the side of the road, so she took the turn wide and crossed the median. Thankfully there were no cars in the oncoming lane.

“Now turn left at the next turn,” Agatha said.

Tori hit the turn signal and came to a stop, waiting for an oncoming car. There was another car behind that one, so she kept waiting. Then there was another car coming at a distance, and maybe she could’ve made the turn before that one, but she wasn’t sure, so she waited again. And again.

“Okay, you’ve got it after this one,” Agatha said finally.

“Are you sure?” Tori asked.

“Yes, I’m sure,” Agatha assured her.

Tori turned. And then she swerved back into her lane because she almost hit the car in the turning lane in the road she was turning onto because she turned too sharp.

“Shit!” Tori exclaimed.

“That’s a bad word,” Ollie said.

“I know, I know,” Tori huffed.

“Okay, sweetheart, no offense, but I’m beginning to see why you haven’t passed your driving test,” Agatha said.

“Ugh!” Tori groaned. “I just… I can’t tell how close I am to things!”

“Hmm… I have an idea,” Agatha said. “Do you think you can get us to the ranch, or do you need to pull over and let me drive?”

“I can do it,” Tori said, determined.

And she did… barely. She took two more turns too sharply going out of town, but once she was on the highway she only crossed the median once, in a curve. She parked her truck in the drive at the ranch and sighed.

“Can I go inside?” Ollie asked.

“Yes, Ollie, you go ahead and go inside,” Agatha told him. “Get a snack and work on your homework. I’m gonna go practice with Tori a little more.”

“Okay,” Ollie nodded, unbuckling his seatbelt. “Good luck, Tori.”

“Thanks, buddy,” Tori sighed.

“C’mon, hop out,” Agatha ordered. Tori climbed out of the driver’s seat, unsure exactly what her mother was planning. Once they were out, Agatha walked over and held out her hand. “Keys.” Tori handed over her keys, but before she could drop her hand, Agatha slipped a key fob into her hand, this one with a silver embossed L in the plastic.

“Wait, these are your keys,” Tori said.

“Duh,” Agatha said.

“I can’t drive your car!” Tori exclaimed.

“Why not?”

“Well— It’s expensive!”

“Yes, it is,” Agatha agreed, reaching for the passenger door handle. “So try not to wreck, okay, hon?”

Tori wanted to argue, but she also knew that it would be pointless. So she threw her hands up in defeat and went around to the driver’s side of the car and got in.

“Why am I so close to the steering wheel?” she groaned.

“Because you inherited your Mami’s long legs,” Agatha huffed. “You adjust the seat with one of the levers on the side.”

Tori adjusted the seat and mirrors, then started the car. It purred to life, and she gripped the wheel tightly.

“Relax, it’s not gonna bite,” Agatha teased.

“I just don’t want to damage anything,” Tori huffed.

“When I was learning to drive, my grandfather got me a truck with a manual transmission and took me to the hill on Spruce Street, you know, the one at the stoplight,” Agatha said. “He told me I would either learn how to change gears, or the truck would roll back into the car behind us.”

“What happened?” Tori asked.

“It didn’t roll back,” Agatha told her. “But I was so focused on the car behind me that I wasn’t looking forward and I drove into a fire hydrant. We had to call the fire department and have them move the car.”

“What did Grandpa say?” Tori asked.

Agatha pursed her lips. “Nothing that bears repeating. He refused to give me any more driving lessons, though. That’s why Lilia ended up teaching me how to drive.”

“What about your mother? Did she ever teach you?” Tori asked.

“Oh, god, no,” Agatha laughed.

In spite of her laughter, Tori thought that was sad. Agatha must’ve picked up on her pity, because she turned to look at her with a serious expression.

“You come from a long line of shitty people, Tori,” she told her. “But that doesn’t mean you have to be like them. Remember that.”

“You’re not so bad,” Tori said with a smirk. She meant for it to be a tease.

“You’re the only one who thinks so,” Agatha said with a bittersweet smile. “Alright, put it in drive and let’s see how you do.”

Tori did as she was told. They stayed on the rural roads at first, as she got used to the sensitivity of the gas pedal and brakes. Then Agatha had her drive into town.

“Okay, turn right up here,” she told her.

Tori put on the turn signal. She slowed down. Then she turned—

“Oh!” Tori exclaimed softly, easing the car into the lane.

“How’d that feel?” Agatha asked.

“So much easier,” Tori replied. “I can see the lines.”

“Mmhmm. Make a left at the stoplight,” Agatha instructed.

Tori did as she was told, and laughed as she did so. She zig-zagged through town, successfully making every turn.

“What do you think?” Agatha asked finally.

“It’s easier in a car, because I’m closer to the road,” Tori surmised.

“I agree,” Agatha nodded. “I can drive a truck when I have to, but it took a lot of practice. That’s why I have a sedan. Well, that and better gas mileage.”

“But you guys already got me a truck,” Tori said.

Agatha shrugged. “We’ll trade it in.”

“Are you sure?” Tori asked. “Don’t I need to know how to drive a truck to run the ranch?”

Agatha’s expression softened. “You— Do you want to run the ranch?”

Tori bit her lip. “I mean… It’s a family business, right? That’s what you told me that day in the cemetery.”

“Yes, that’s right,” Agatha nodded.

“And I understand if you just want Nicky and Ollie to have it. I just thought—”

“Tori, you’re just as much my child as Nicky and Ollie are,” Agatha said. “Of course I want you to have part of taking on the ranch, as you get older. It’ll be yours someday, the three of you. I just didn’t realize it might be something that you want, too.”

“I think so,” Tori told her. “I know I have a lot to learn. But I love the horses, I like the cows, and this place is just… I love it here, Mama.”

“I’m so glad, sweetie.” Agatha wiped at her eyes, and Tori realized she was crying. “I just hope there’s something left for you to inherit someday.”

Tori turned toward home. Her brow wrinkled in confusion. “What do you mean?”

“Well, times are changing,” Agatha sighed. “Ranching is a hard business. Every year it gets harder and harder to break even, much less make a profit.”

“So… maybe you should branch out into other income streams,” Tori suggested.

“What do you mean?” Agatha asked.

“Well, I follow a lot of online influencers who bring in lots of income from posting about their animals and their business,” Tori told her.

“I don’t know how I feel about putting our business on the internet,” Agatha replied.

“Yeah, but you can decide what gets published and what doesn’t,” Tori shrugged. “Another thing you could look at is agritourism.”

“Agri-what now?”

Tori grinned. “Agritourism. Diversification. I was thinking something along the lines of using part of the ranch as an entertainment venue for weddings and such.”

“You were thinking, huh?” Agatha smirked. “You’ve been thinking about this?”

“I was thinking that someday, when I get married, it would be cool to get married on the ranch,” Tori shrugged. “And then I started thinking that other people might like that, too. If there’s any part of the ranch that isn’t actively being used for cattle, you might look at turning it into a usable space for something like that.”

Agatha looked at her fondly as they pulled back into the drive to the ranch. “You’re so fucking smart.”

Tori blushed. “I mean… I have you and Mami as my moms. It was kind of inevitable.”

“That’s very true,” Agatha agreed. “That is very true.”

Chapter 20: Agatha

Chapter Summary

Parent Trap: Stage 2

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“I can’t believe you got a Subaru.”

Agatha looked up from her sudoku puzzle book. Beside her, in the driver’s seat, Rio glanced up into the rearview mirror and smirked.

A four hour road trip with three kids and your ex might’ve been hell to other people, but they were three hours into the drive and so far it had been surprisingly uneventful. They picked the kids up early from school, loaded up the horses, threw their bags in the back of the truck, and hit the road. All three kids were sandwiched in the backseat of the truck, with Tori behind Agatha, Nicky behind Rio, and Ollie in his booster seat between the two of them. Agatha had worried that Ollie might get overwhelmed being smooshed between his sisters, but he had fallen asleep an hour into the drive and was now leaning into Tori, drooling on her shoulder. Everything had been peaceful, until Nicky started picking at her sister about her new car.

“Subaru is a reliable brand,” Tori argued.

“It’s also the official car brand of lesbians,” Nicky pointed out. Agatha had to bite back a laugh, and beside her Rio actually snorted but tried to cover it with a cough.

“So?” Tori shrugged. “I am a lesbian.”

“Nicky, hon, have you forgotten that you’re the only straight woman in this car right now?” Agatha asked.

“I’m just saying that she didn’t have to play into the stereotype,” Nicky said.

“It’s not my fault lesbians have good taste in cars,” Tori told her.

“That is definitely questionable,” Nicky argued.

Tori sat up straighter in her seat, jostling Ollie slightly, but he only turned his head further into her shoulder.

“Monica liked it,” Tori said, a slight grin on her lips.

Rio glanced up into the mirror again and grinned.

“Who’s Monica?” Agatha asked.

“Tori’s new girlfriend,” Nicky replied in a sing-song voice.

“She’s not my girlfriend,” Tori groaned, then mumbled, “yet.”

“After her driving test, she asked to go get a milkshake to celebrate,” Rio elaborated. “I thought we were just going for a sweet treat, turns out Tori is sweet on more than just the ice cream.”

“She said my car was really cool,” Tori beamed.

Nicky rolled her eyes. “Well, that was a lie.”

“Next time I go to the diner, I’m gonna ask if she wants to hang out sometime,” Tori told them.

“Is that Gen Z speak for ask her out on a date?” Rio asked.

Tori blushed. “Yes.”

“Good for you!” Agatha said, patting her daughter’s knee. She looked toward Nicky. “While we’re on the subject—”

“No,” Nicky grumbled.

“I have it on good authority from a certain redheaded school secretary that her son has a crush on you,” Agatha continued.

“I thought Wanda’s son was gay?” Rio asked.

“She got a two for one deal,” Agatha replied. “Twins.”

“I’ve mentioned Tommy before,” Tori said, frowning.

“Honestly, mija, you’ve made so many new friends that sometimes I forget their names. I’m sorry,” Rio said.

“Yeah, Tori’s friends are really great,” Nicky agreed. “They’re—”

Nicky crossed her arms. “There’s nothing to spill. He’s Morgan’s ex.”

“I know,” Nicky sighed.

“Mija, if you don’t like him back, it’s okay,” Rio spoke up.

“Hah! I knew it!” Tori exclaimed victoriously.

“But he’s my friend!” Nicky argued. “What if we start dating and it doesn’t work out? That would be so awkward. I don’t want to mess things up.”

“But what if it does work out?” Tori argued.

Agatha glanced at Rio, but the other woman was staring pointedly out the windshield at the oncoming traffic.

“What do you like about him?” Agatha asked, turning her attention back to her daughter.

“He’s such a dork,” Nicky huffed. “Everybody thinks he’s this cool track star, but he’s really just a big golden retriever. How would I not like him?”

“I mean, he’s a dude, so…” Tori trailed off.

“Well, I like dudes,” Nicky said.

“I can’t believe we made a straight kid,” Rio commented.

“Tell me about it,” Agatha agreed.

“You guys are so weird,” Nicky told them.

“Guilty as charged, mija,” Rio nodded.


One drive thru stop for dinner and another hour of driving later, they made it to the event center where the rodeo was being held. Agatha helped the girls get their horses settled in the stalls in the livestock building while Rio took Ollie with her to park the trailer in the overnight lot. Once the girls were registered and Luna and Scratchy were fed and settled in for the night, they met Rio and Ollie back at the truck and headed to the hotel.

The girls had been chatterboxes the entire time they were at the arena, but they got quieter as they drew closer to the hotel. Agatha should’ve suspected some kind of mischief was afoot. But she was distracted by the ongoing conversation Rio and Ollie were having about chickens and dinosaurs.

“Mama, tell her!” Ollie argued, yanking on Agatha’s hand as they made their way into the hotel lobby.

“I don’t care what anyone says, I don’t believe you,” Rio said, feigning stubbornness.

“But I’m serious!” Ollie insisted. “Velociraptors had feathers just like chickens!”

“I still think they looked like the ones in Jurassic Park,” Rio said.

Ollie kicked the toe of his sneakers across the tile floor. “Stupid Steven Spielburg.”

Agatha smirked as she stepped toward the reception desk. The bottle blonde behind the counter looked up at her with a smile. “Hello. Checking in?”

“Yes, the reservation is under Harkness,” Agatha answered.

The blonde typed away on her computer. “Yes, ma’am, I have two connected rooms booked under Harkness, both are king suites, and a roll-away twin bed—”

“Two suites?” Agatha interrupted.

“Yes, ma’am,” the hostess nodded.

“I booked three rooms,” Agatha corrected. “Two king suites and one double room.”

The hostess clicked on her computer again. “My records show that you did book two king suites and a double room, ma’am, but that reservation was changed and the double room cancelled.”

“Cancelled? But who—” Agatha bit her tongue. She turned around to see Nicky and Tori standing behind Rio, looking anywhere but at her. “My apologies. I need to add the double room back, please.”

“I’m sorry, ma’am, but that won’t be possible,” the hostess replied.

“What?” Agatha exclaimed, turning back to the woman.

“We’re completely booked up because of the rodeo,” the blonde told her. “I would be happy to accommodate you if there were any double rooms available, but unfortunately I don’t have any.”

“Great,” Agatha huffed. “We’ll make it work.”

“Wonderful,” the hostess smiled. “I’ll just get your keycards.”

Agatha rubbed her temple. She was going to kill her daughters.

“What happened?” Rio asked, her whispered question startling Agatha so much that she nearly jumped out of her skin, hitting her knee against the counter with a loud thump.

“Son of a— biscuit,” Agatha exclaimed through gritted teeth. She glared at Rio. “Your daughters changed our reservation, so instead of three rooms, we have two king suites.”

Rio’s brow shot up. “Oh, they’re my daughters when they’re being sneaky?”

“Yes,” Agatha replied.

“I feel like that’s something you would do,” Rio told her with a smirk. Agatha glared at her. “It’s fine. Tori and I can take one room and you and Nicky and Ollie can take the other—”

“No!” Nicky whined.

“Mami, please, I want to share with Nicky!” Tori begged.

“Girls—” Agatha began.

“Ollie can stay with us, too!” Nicky argued. “You and Mami can have a peaceful night’s sleep.”

Agatha highly doubted it would be peaceful. She opened her mouth to argue again, but Rio cut around her to speak to the woman at the desk.

“Hi, excuse me,” Rio said, drawing the hostess’s attention.

“Oh— hi,” the blonde said, her cheeks flushing as she looked Rio up and down. Agatha felt her hackles rise, but Rio just grinned that crooked grin at the woman.

“You wouldn’t happen to have any more of those twin roll-away beds, would you?”

“I’m sorry, we’re fresh out,” the blonde replied.

“Oh,” Rio said, her face falling. “Is there anything else to sleep on in the king suite besides the bed?”

“There’s a pull-out couch in each of the king suites, yes,” the hostess told her. “I can have extra sheets sent up if you’d like.”

“That would be wonderful, thank you,” Rio said with a wink.

A wink.

She fucking winked at her—

“Problem solved,” Rio said. “I’ll sleep on the pull-out sofa. The kids can share the other room.”

“Oh,” Tori said, looking disappointed.

“Okay,” Nicky agreed.

“I thought you guys wanted to have a sleepover?” Rio asked, raising a brow. “If you’re disappointed, then Tori can stay with me and—”

“No!” Tori exclaimed.

“No, this is fine,” Nicky agreed.

“That’s what I thought,” Rio said, rolling her eyes.

The rooms, at least, were spacious once they got into them. They were mirrors of each other, with a bathroom and small closet, a sitting area with a sofa and a desk, and then a king size bed and dresser with a flatscreen television over it. There was a door connecting the two rooms, and each room had a balcony overlooking the pool below and the mountains in the distance. There was a rollaway twin bed folded in the corner of one room which Rio easily unfolded for Ollie to sleep on.

“Alright, well, if everyone is settled, I’m going to go shower,” Agatha declared, watching as Rio and Nicky set about putting sheets on the smaller bed. “Goodnight!”

She didn’t need a shower. In fact, she wasn’t due to wash her hair for another day at least. But she needed to delay being stuck in the same room with Rio for the night.

A room with only one bed.

Agatha opened her suitcase on the bed and started digging through her clothes. She found her pajamas, an oversized t-shirt and shorts. Had she known that she would be sharing a room with Rio, she would’ve packed actual pajamas, something with more structure. Once she had her clothing picked out, she grabbed her toiletry bag and took everything to the bathroom. She set out her toothbrush, her makeup, her deodorant, her facewash, her shamp—

She had no shampoo. She didn’t have conditioner either. Agatha dumped the rest of the contents from her bag onto the counter— hairbrush, comb, hair gel, heat-protection spray, lotion, sunscreen, perfume, bodywash— but no shampoo or conditioner.

“Motherfucker!” she roared. She could picture the bottles in her mind’s eye, sitting on her bathroom counter where she had filled them up and set them aside so she wouldn’t forget them.

There was a knock at the door. “Hey, everything okay in there?”

Agatha sighed and opened the door a crack. “I forgot to pack my shampoo and conditioner.”

“Oh,” Rio said with a grin. “I thought you fell and broke your hip or something.”

“Haha,” Agatha deadpanned. “Guess I’ll use the hotel brand.”

Rio narrowed her eyes. “Ew, no. You can use mine.”

Agatha wasn’t thrilled about using the hotel brand, either, because she knew it would dry out her hair, but she wasn’t sure Rio’s would be any better. Last time she had known Rio, the woman was using Herbal Essences and thought it was high quality.

The pillow smelled like Rio. Her hair smelled like Rio.

Agatha groaned and rolled over to stare up at the ceiling.

She was fucked.

Chapter 21: Rio

Chapter Summary

The rodeo, an accident, and a dance

Chapter Notes

CW: horseback riding related injury, talk of premature childbirth and NICU

Also please check out the art by beccsvibes, inspired by a scene in this chapter!

“Mami, you don’t look so good.”

Rio raised her head and looked blearily across the table at her daughters. They wore matching expressions of concern as they studied her. Rio knew exactly what she looked like— wrinkled shirt, damp hair, and dark circles under her eyes.

She finished chewing her food and cleared her throat. “I’m fine. Didn’t sleep much last night, that’s all.”

Normally Rio would be exhausted after driving such a long distance, and last night had been no different. But after six weeks of sleeping in Agatha’s guest bed, the hotel’s pullout bed had been uncomfortable as hell. Combine that with the fact that Agatha was lying only a few feet away, and Rio had been restless. The problem with being restless, however, was that whenever Rio moved an inch the metal bedframe would creak loudly. So in order to not disturb Agatha, Rio had done her best to avoid moving altogether.

She was stiff and tired and cranky as hell. And the teenage girls exchanging not-so-secretive grins across the table from her weren’t helping the situation.

“I know what you two are up to, and you need to back off,” Rio growled, sipping her coffee. The hotel coffee was over-brewed and bitter, but she was willing to drink straight caffeine if it would wake her up.

“We don’t know what you’re talking about,” Nicky said, batting her eyelashes.

“Yeah, Mami, you shouldn’t be so—” Tori began.

“Cut it,” Rio barked. “You’re meddling where you don’t need to meddle. The relationship between your mama and I is friendly and that’s it, nothing more. ¿Lo entiendes?”

“Sí, Mami,” Tori nodded, looking down at her plate.

“Sure, yeah,” Nicky agreed.

Their breakfast was interrupted a moment later as Agatha swept into the dining room with Ollie in tow. The boy had had a meltdown over the hotel’s complimentary breakfast having waffles but no pancakes because texture, so Agatha had taken him across the street to a cafe and ordered pancakes to go. He sat down beside Nicky with his to-go box and started eating as if it was no big deal.

“I got coffees for everyone, too,” Agatha announced, placing the drink tray on the table. “Iced mocha for Tori, iced caramel latte for Nicky, and a vanilla latte with two shots of espresso for Mami.”

Rio immediately pushed aside her hotel coffee and took the cup from Agatha. As soon as the strong brew and vanilla flavor hit her taste buds she moaned in appreciation.

“God, I love you,” she mumbled, eyes still closed.
