“I’m telling you this because ever since Rio and Tori left, this place doesn’t feel like freedom anymore,” Agatha said, her voice breaking with emotion. “It doesn’t even feel like chains.”

“What does it feel like?” Nicky asked.

“It feels like a noose. And it’s suffocating me,” Agatha admitted.

Nicky wrapped her arms around Agatha’s shoulders, and Agatha leaned into her daughter, letting Nicky be the one to hold her up for once.

Agatha let out a sound that was somewhere between a laugh and a sob at the question. Leave it to her daughter to get to the root of the issue.

“Does this mean we’re moving back to the ranch?” Tori asked, her eyes bright with excitement and relief at the thought.

“Well, we hadn’t really talked about it,” Rio replied, fastening her pants and looking around at Agatha.

“Of course you didn’t,” Nicky muttered, crossing her arms.

“I was actually considering selling the ranch and moving here with you and Mami,” Agatha declared.

“What?” Rio and Tori exclaimed at the same time.

“Agatha—” Rio began.

“No, listen,” Agatha said, placing a placating hand on Rio’s arm. “I’ve been thinking about it, and it’s not fair that I’ve always expected you to give up everything to make this work. If this job here in California is what you want, then we’ll make it work.”

Rio placed her hand on top of Agatha’s, squeezing lightly. “The fact that you’re even willing to do that means everything to me, my love. You know that. But, um… It’s completely unnecessary.”

“What do you mean?” Agatha asked.

Rio shrugged. “Turns out that everything I thought I wanted wasn’t actually here. It was back home, in Westview, with you.”

Across the room, Tori sniffled loudly. “I’m gonna cry.”

“I’m gonna puke,” Nicky muttered.

Agatha’s eyes suddenly filled up with tears, but her lips spread into a wide smile. “I don’t want to ask you to give up your dreams again.”

“You’re not,” Rio assured her. “Sometimes… dreams change.”

Chapter 31: Epilogue

Chapter Summary

Ten Years Later

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Tori flitted around the barn, making sure everything was perfect for the reception. Outside, the guests were just starting to arrive and the musicians were warming up. The officiant was running behind, but so was the bridal party, so maybe that was for the best.

“Did you know that’s the third time you’ve adjusted that particular flower arrangement?”

Tori nearly jumped out of her skin. “Oliver James Harkness-Vidal! Do not sneak up on me like that!”

Ollie just smirked at her. He was a head taller than her now, though his full cheeks and dimples still gave him boyish charm. His long hair was held back in a low ponytail, and he wore a sharply pressed white button-up with his nicest pair of jeans for the wedding.

“I just want everything to be perfect,” Tori huffed, moving to fluff one of the nearby flower arrangements. “This wedding’s been a long time coming.”

“I never thought they’d get their heads out of their asses,” Ollie agreed.

Tori gave a fake, dramatic gasp. “Ollie! Do you kiss your mother with that mouth?”

“I kiss both our mothers with this mouth,” Ollie said dryly. Tori just rolled her eyes at his humor. “Seriously, sis, everything looks perfect. You’ve outdone yourself.”

Tori flushed at his praise. Ever since she graduated college with a degree in business and marketing, she had worked to reinvigorate the ranch’s portfolio. While Agatha still managed most of the livestock part of the business, she had given Tori free rein to grow other aspects of the business. Tori had taken over the old Stark vineyard and worked to transform the barn there into an event venue for dances and weddings. This would be its first official debut.

“You know what you need?” Ollie asked, reaching into his pocket. He pulled out a silver flask and unscrewed the lid. He offered it to Tori, and her stomach turned as the smell of whiskey hit her nose.

“No thanks,” she said, hoping she didn’t look as green as she felt. “And where the hell did you get that? You’re eighteen!”

Ollie didn’t answer, just took a sip from the flask, then put it back in his pocket. Tori moved onto the next arrangement, fixing the placement of a sprig of eucalyptus before moving to the next one. Ollie’s eyes followed her the entire time.

“What?” she asked finally.

“Nothing,” he said. He stepped closer to her and leaned down to whisper in her ear. “Does Monica know?”

Tori’s eyes widened. “Does Monica know what?”

“About my niece or nephew,” Ollie said smugly.

“I— Wh— I don’t know what—” Tori began, only for his facial expression to silence her argument. “How did you know?”

He shrugged. “I watch people. I know things. You refused champagne at brunch this morning, you almost puked when you smelled the omelets I made yesterday—”

“That’s because you cook like a frat boy,” Tori argued, but Ollie just stared at her in a way that was far too similar to their Mama. “Okay, fine… No, Monica doesn’t know yet. I found out just after she was deployed on this training mission. But it’s only a six-week program, so I’m waiting until she gets back to tell her.” She glared at him and raised a finger in warning. “So you’d better keep your mouth shut, little brother.”

Ollie raised his hand to his face and pretended to zip his lips, turn a key in a lock, and throw away the key. “My lips are sealed.”

“Good,” Tori said, turning toward the door. A frazzled looking old man stood there, and she smiled. “Looks like Hank is here. Let’s get this show on the road.”



Rio stared at the scene in front of her. Nicky looked absolutely gorgeous in her flowing lace dress. Her hair was done up in a loose updo, and as Rio watched, Agatha helped place her veil over her head, the same veil that Agatha had worn when she and Rio got married several years before.

“Don’t cry, Mama,” Nicky whined. “If you start crying, I’m gonna cry, and then they’re gonna have to redo our makeup again.”

“I can’t help it,” Agatha insisted. “You look so beautiful.”

Nicky rolled her eyes. “Mami, help me out here.”

“She’s not wrong, mija. You look beautiful,” Rio said, her own eyes damp.

Tori hurried up the stairs at that moment, her pale turquoise jumpsuit flowing with each movement. “Hank is here! I think everyone’s ready!”

“Is Tommy ready?” Nicky asked.

“That boy’s been ready,” Rio muttered. Agatha agreed.

After asking her out for the first time at the bonfire party, Tommy had respected Nicky’s request that they just stay friends. Then he had asked her to go to prom with him, and she had agreed— but only as friends. They went to college, and they stayed in touch, but Nicky insisted that they were just friends. Then Nicky went to vet school, and they talked almost every day, but they still weren’t dating. It was only once she finished vet school that Nicky agreed to be Tommy’s girlfriend. That had rapidly evolved to her being Tommy’s fiance just a few months later, and now, barely a year after graduating from vet school, they were getting married.

Rio had her suspicions about why that was, but she was keeping her mouth shut for now.

They made their way down the stairs of the guest cabin and found Ollie waiting outside with the horses. They had decided months before that it was only fitting that they would all ride to the wedding on horseback. Nicky had specifically chosen a dress that she could ride in comfortably for that reason. Nicky, of course, rode Scratchy, who had been bathed until his white patches gleamed and then had flowers braided into his mane. Agatha still rode River, though the mare was getting on in years, and Ollie rode one of her offspring, a bay-roan stallion named Rooster. Rio rode Luna, Lady having passed away several years before. Tori rode a bay paint colt, the youngest of the herd, named Orion. Luna was his dam, and Scratchy was his sire.

They made their way toward the barn, Ollie beside Tori, Agatha and Rio on either side of Nicky. As they drew closer they could hear the string quartet playing softly. When they were just a few yards away, Dr. McCoy, who had gotten his officiant license for Agatha and Rio’s wedding a decade earlier, asked the small crowd to stand. They dismounted at the back of the crowd and several ranchhands were on hand to take the horses from them— not Lilia, because she was somewhere near the front of the crowd with Jen and Alice. Ollie and Tori walked down the aisle as the music swelled, and then Rio stepped to Nicky’s side and took her arm.

Agatha stood on their daughter’s other side, holding her other hand. They glanced at each other with a soft, secret smile, before turning and walking down the aisle.

Rio looked to the front of the ceremony space, where the bridegroom was waiting under an arch of pink roses and purple lavender and white wildflowers. Tommy’s eyes were on Nicky, and he was looking at her the same way Rio looked at Agatha: like she was his sunshine. That was all they could ever want for their daughter.

When they reached the end of the aisle, Agatha folded Nicky’s veil back out of her face and kissed her cheek. Rio kissed her other cheek before placing her hands in Tommy’s.

They sat beside each other in the spindly folding chairs and listened as Hank welcomed everyone and waxed poetic about how wonderful love was and how perfect Nicky and Tommy were for each other. Then came the moment for the vows, and Agatha expected the traditional to have and to hold, for better or worse, for richer or poorer, in sickness and in health, to love and to cherish. She was surprised when Agatha leaned closer to whisper in her ear, speaking in unison with Nicky.

“I vow to choose you, every day, over all others. I choose you to share in my sorrows and my joys. I choose you to grow old with. I choose you, for all that you are. I choose to love you, Rio Vidal, for the rest of my life.”

Nicky, of course, had said Tommy’s name. But the intent was the same.

Rio turned to Agatha in surprise and whispered, “They used our vows? The ones we wrote?”

At the altar, Tommy was repeating the same words. Beside her, Agatha nodded. “They tried to write their own, but they liked ours the best. I told them we didn’t mind.”

“Tori and Monica used them, too,” Rio noted as Tommy and Nicky exchanged rings.

“By the power vested in me by the great state of Montana, it is my honor and privilege to declare you husband and wife,” Hank declared happily. “You may now kiss the bride!”

As Nicky and Tommy kissed, Agatha turned and pressed a quick kiss to Rio’s cheek.

“I love you, Mrs. Harkness-Vidal,” Agatha whispered.

“And I love you, Mrs. Harkness-Vidal,” Rio replied, smiling proudly back at her.



The reception was just starting to wind down when Nicky finally managed to get away from all the well-wishers. She and Tommy had barely even had time to eat, between taking photos and the first dance, opening gifts, and speaking to all the guests. She desperately wanted a glass of champagne or, even better, a sip of whatever Ollie was carrying around in the flask that he wasn’t supposed to have, but unfortunately that was out of the question.

She finally found the person she was searching for upstairs, in the loft above the barn. Tori was leaning against the garland-wrapped railing, looking down at the dancefloor. Most of the dancers had left the floor when the song switched from a line dance to a slow song, but one couple remained. Their mothers held each other close as they swayed to the music. As they watched, Agatha took the cowboy hat from Rio’s head and put it on her own and laughed. Their mothers might be older now, the lines in their faces a bit deeper, but they were still the same deep down, and just as in love as they had ever been.

“They’re disgusting,” Nicky said, leaning on the railing beside Tori. Below them, their mothers kissed unabashedly, tongue and all, in front of all the wedding guests. “Do you think we’ll be like that in thirty years or so?”

“I hope so,” Tori replied. Her sister looked at her with fond blue eyes. “Was your wedding day everything you hoped it would be?”

“Better,” Nicky assured her. “You did an amazing job. This place is amazing. You really made something special here, Tori. This is going to be a great thing for the ranch.”

Her sister’s cheeks flushed. “Thank you.”

“I mean, it wasn’t Vegas…” Nicky teased.

“Excuse me! There were extenuating circumstances!” Tori exclaimed.

Nicky laughed. Tori and Monica had eloped to Vegas before Monica’s first deployment. It had all been very dramatic. Their families had thrown a celebration when Monica came back home, but it hadn’t been quite the same as a wedding. Personally, Nicky thought the pictures the two had with the Dolly Parton drag queen officiant were worth it.

“I still say a fall wedding would’ve been even prettier,” Tori pointed out. “And we wouldn’t be sweating bullets right now.

Nicky sighed. “I know I made it difficult by moving up the timeline.”

“But you couldn’t help it that you got that opportunity to travel to Nepal next month,” Tori argued. “I’m still jealous that you get to go work with tigers.”

Nicky blushed. “Yeah, well… I would’ve done it after I got back, but there were… extenuating circumstances.”

Tori stared at her in confusion. “What?”

Nicky sipped the sparkling cider in her champagne glass. “Nothing. I do have a question for you though.”

“What?” Tori asked nervously.

“How far along are you?”

“Well, I’m not exactly sure but— Hey!” Tori exclaimed. She looked down at the crowd below until she found where their brother was sitting with Tommy and Billy. “Ollie, you little shit!”

“Ollie didn’t tell me,” Nicky chuckled.

“Then how did you—?”

“Let’s just say the symptoms are easy to spot when you’re also experiencing them.”

Tori stared at her for a moment before her brain processed the information. “No!”

“Yep,” Nicky nodded. “I’m thirteen weeks tomorrow. You?”

“Nine weeks I think,” Tori replied.

Nicky laughed again. “Oh, Mami and Mama are gonna freak out.”

“Do you think they know?” Tori asked.

“Nah,” Nicky replied. “I don’t think they’ve noticed.”



Agatha sat in front of her vanity, brushing the tangles from the still-damp ends of her hair. It was almost two in the morning. Nicky and Tommy were on the way to the airport for their honeymoon, Tori was crashing in the girls’ old bedroom, and Ollie had only made it to the living room sofa before falling asleep. Rio had graciously allowed Agatha to shower first, and as she brushed her hair Agatha heard the water turn off in the other room. She turned in her seat, watching through the open door as her wife stepped out of the shower in a cloud of steam. Rio toweled her skin dry before wrapping herself in the towel and turning to catch Agatha ogling her.

“See something you like?” Rio asked.

“You better believe it, cowgirl,” Agatha replied.

Rio smirked and went to the bathroom sink to finish getting ready for bed. She combed and dried her hair a bit before getting out her toothbrush and toothpaste.

“I’m still mad that Nicky took his last name,” Agatha said finally.

“She’s keeping Harkness-Vidal professionally,” Rio told her. “But they wanted to keep the Maximoff name going.”

“I can’t believe my grandchildren are going to have the last name Maximoff,” Agatha grumbled. “And goodness knows what last name Tori and Monica will give their children. They have four to choose from.”

“At least we have Ollie to carry on the Harkness-Vidal moniker,” Rio said.

Agatha beamed at her. When Ollie was thirteen, he had asked Rio to officially adopt him, and they had legally changed his last name in the process. As far as any of them were concerned, he was just as much Rio’s kid as Nicky and Tori.

“Let’s not talk about my baby boy getting married, please,” Agatha begged. “He’s only eighteen, I’m not quite ready to let him go yet.”

“Fair enough,” Rio agreed. She decided not to tell her wife about the flask she had taken from their son at the wedding, instead changing the subject. “Are you ready to be a grandma yet?”

Agatha snorted. “No. But I don’t think we have much of a choice at this point, do we?”

“Nope,” Rio said, putting her toothbrush away. She stepped behind Agatha at the vanity and reached around to stroke the one streak of gray hair that grew from her temple. “You’ve got the gray hairs for the title.”

“Oh, you!” Agatha hissed, slapping the back of her hand with the hairbrush. Rio just laughed at her, retreating to the dresser to get her pajamas. Agatha watched her, openly ogling her ass as she changed.

“Can you believe they think we don’t know yet?” Rio asked. She caught Agatha looking at her again. “Hey! Eyes up here, you pervert.”

Agatha rolled her eyes at her wife. “Tori has spent every morning for the last two weeks bent over the toilet. Nicky suddenly added sparkling cider to the wedding drink list as if we wouldn’t notice. Do they not realize that we’ve been in their shoes before?”

“They’ll tell us when they’re ready,” Rio said, getting into bed. “Do you think you can act surprised?”

Agatha turned around with feign shock. “Me? A grandma? I can’t believe it!”

Rio chuckled. “Truly an Oscar-worthy performance, mi amor.”

“Thank you, thank you,” Agatha said, standing and bowing as she made her way to the bed. She crawled under the covers and into Rio’s arms. “What do you think of becoming an abuelita?”

Rio’s breath caught in her throat. “I think it’s gonna be an adventure. But I can’t wait. And I can’t wait to see our girls as mothers.”

“Oh god, they’re going to be mothers! And we're going to be grandmothers!” Agatha exclaimed, the full reality of it hitting her. Tears welled up in her eyes, and she quickly wiped them away.

“I know, it’s crazy,” Rio agreed.

Agatha looked at Rio with awe. “Did you ever think we’d end up here?”

Rio gave her a bittersweet smile. “Sometimes I doubted it. But I always hoped we would.”

Agatha smiled and nestled further into her wife's embrace. "Goodnight, Mrs. Harkness-Vidal."

Rio pressed a kiss to her forehead. "Goodnight, my love."

Chapter End Notes

This fic has been such a labor of love. I am so sad to come to the end with these versions of Agatha and Rio, and especially Nicky, Tori, and Ollie. But I feel like Agatha and Rio becoming grandmas is the perfect end to their story.
If you haven’t, please check out the art that goes along with this fic. The artists I was matched with are so talented it’s absolutely insane.
